London Chinese Society Hosts Banquet for Central Celebrities Ambassador Guo Delivers Speech on Relations between the Two Countries 36

(London) Tonight, the Chinese Society held a banquet, and many Chinese and British celebrities attended. Ambassador Guo Taiqi presided over the meeting. Among the guests were the Earl and Countess of Winterton, the Earl and Countess of Iveagh, former British Minister to China Sir Miles Lampson and his wife, the President of the Royal Academy of Arts Sir William Llewellyn, Conservative Party Member of Parliament Mr. Lunn, who often asks about Far East issues in the House of Commons, and world-renowned writer H.G. Wells. When Ambassador Guo raised his glass to wish the guests longevity, he said that Sino-British relations have now reached a turning point. In the past, British people always felt a half-hidden contempt for the Far East, while Chinese people often felt that Western trade doctrines were heavily oppressive. But today, these are all things of the past. China and Britain have known each other for a long time, but it may be difficult to understand to what extent they have now reached cooperation between the two countries. Wells replied that the era of making vague generalizations about East and West has completely passed. In the past, people thought of China as a vague land of gods, immortals, and ghosts, but radio airplanes and other inventions have made the distance of thousands of miles seem like a stone's throw away. Therefore, people are increasingly aware that they share a common destiny. Our languages and thoughts are different, so we must work to understand them. If I had several lifetimes, I would use one of them to translate Chinese philosophy. Britain, the United States, and China all have a common understanding of freedom, so they can form a closely united group. All three countries hate the world drifting towards narrow-mindedness and aggression. This is indeed a bond of enviable sympathy among us. The history of the next hundred years may be a history of fierce struggles to fight for freedom. Therefore, we should not regard each other as strangers, but as friends and brothers. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

British Foreign Secretary Explains Foreign Policy to the House of Commons Willing to Redeem the Crisis According to the Principles of the League of Nations Does Not Want to Impose Individual Threats on Italy Anglo-German Naval Agreement is by No Means a Selfish Contract Maintains Friendly Relations with Japan in the Far East 45

This afternoon, the House of Commons will debate diplomatic events. Foreign Secretary Hoare will review many issues, such as the Italo-Abyssinian crisis and the Anglo-German naval talks. Liberal Party Samuel, Labor Party Attlee, former Finance Minister Churchill, and Conservative Party Winterton will speak to express the views of various parties. Unaffiliated member Eden will represent the government to conclude the debate. (Reuters, 11th)

(London) British officials are deeply concerned that efforts to salvage the Italo-Abyssinian war will ultimately fail, but the peace movement is still underway in an extremely bleak atmosphere. The cabinet met today to draft an important statement in preparation for Foreign Secretary Hoare to read to the House of Commons tomorrow. (National Telegram, 11th)

(Paris) This afternoon, the eyes of the French will be focused on London, hoping to obtain clues about Anglo-French cooperation to eliminate the Italo-Abyssinian war. Optimists believe that after Britain announced that it would not take individual action, there may be cooperation between Britain and France. (Reuters, 11th)

(Rome) People here are paying great attention to the British policy on this matter that will be expressed by the British House of Commons in London this afternoon. (Reuters, 11th)

(London) This afternoon, when British Foreign Secretary Hoare debated diplomatic events in the House of Commons, he mentioned the Italo-Abyssinian crisis, saying that we are now working to salvage the catastrophe by means of the 1906 treaty and the League of Nations. We have not asked France to join in the blockade imposed on Italy, nor are we prepared to implement individual threats against Italy. What we want is to maintain the principles on which the League of Nations was founded. This is why we attach importance to this dispute. We have no other purpose but to see a peaceful resolution. We are well aware of Italy's desire for overseas development and recognize the legitimacy of its accusations against the Abyssinian government on several matters. But is the need for development and some accusations sufficient reason to start a war?

During the debate, the public gallery of the House of Commons was very crowded. The ambassadors and many ministers from France, Italy, Germany, Russia, and China, and eight other countries were present to listen. The debate began at 3:40 pm. Foreign Secretary Hoare spoke first, describing the terrible state of the world left by the last great war, and asked Britain to use its goodwill and common sense to consider its foreign policy. Foreign Secretary Hoare continued to say that the Anglo-German naval agreement is by no means a selfish contract, and he believes that this matter is also beneficial to other naval countries and will eventually promote a universal convention. He is confident that the great powers all want to avoid linking the naval issue with land and air disarmament. In our view, for the sake of peace, we certainly have sufficient reason to establish such an agreement. We therefore take peace as our main objective. When the agreement was not yet established, the German authorities issued important remarks, stating that Germany would abolish the unrestricted attacks of submarines on merchant ships. This promise is obviously also beneficial to naval countries such as France. The Anglo-German naval agreement has given France a permanent advantage, because before the war the French navy was 30% weaker than the German navy, and from now on the French navy will be 43% stronger than the German navy. The Foreign Secretary also said that if we negotiate the air convention alone, without linking it to any other issues, then the British people, having satisfied their current needs, will have no concern for other issues on which European peace depends. The Foreign Secretary later mentioned Britain's policy in the Far East, saying that we attach great importance to friendly relations with Japan, which goes without saying. Our Japanese friends in Britain are quite disturbed by recent events in North China. He made this remark to show that we are honest and open with our Japanese friends. He hopes that this tense scene has now ended, and that our desire for friendly relations with Japan can have a more complete and unrestricted opportunity. (Reuters, 11th)

Anglo-French Continued Talks Seeking Peaceful Resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian Dispute 46

(Havas, 10th)

No More Than Two Ways to Resolve 47

(London) Regarding the resolution of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, negotiations are underway among Britain, France, and Italy. It is generally believed that there are no more than two ways to resolve it: (1) To enable Italy to obtain substantial benefits in Abyssinia by peaceful means; (2) To have Abyssinia withdraw its request to the League of Nations for a resolution of the dispute. As for the attitude of the British government, it has changed since last week, because it is difficult to obtain unanimous approval from the Executive Council to impose economic sanctions on Italy in accordance with Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant, so this is difficult to achieve. Moreover, the Conservative Party strongly opposes an excessively anti-Italian policy, so the government's attitude must change somewhat. All parties in Britain believe that it is better for Britain to help the League of Nations out of this difficult situation than to mediate the dispute on behalf of the League of Nations. Therefore, Britain's new strategy should be on how not to expose the League of Nations' weakness and how to eliminate the conflict of opinions among the member states of the League of Nations, so that the authority of the League of Nations will not be lost. For this reason, the British government has started negotiations with France and Italy on the one hand, and has sought the opinions of League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol on the other hand. The outcome of the negotiations is still unknown at this time, but it is generally believed that the various possible solutions stipulated in the 1906 Anglo-French-Italian treaty on Abyssinia have not been fully utilized so far. The 1906 treaty stipulated that the signatory countries could consult each other to establish a new system in the territories previously agreed upon as the spheres of influence of each country. From this, it seems that after the League of Nations Executive Council announced the failure of the Italo-Abyssinian arbitration committee, it could request the signatory countries to the 1906 three-nation treaty to resolve the Italo-Abyssinian dispute in accordance with the above-mentioned method. However, this resolution method can only be decided after the three countries, Britain, France, and Italy, hold preliminary talks and reach a consensus. At present, there are about two main difficulties in the preliminary talks: first, Italy has various political and economic demands in addition to the control of the territories it demands; second, because Abyssinia is also a member state of the League of Nations, it is factually difficult to hand Abyssinia over to Italy for mandate rule. Regarding the second point, it is generally believed that Italy can adopt another method of managing Abyssinian territory. There is a precedent for this in the League of Nations. For example, Iraq is actually managed by Britain, but nominally it is a suzerain state and a member state of the League of Nations. Abyssinia may as well do the same in the future. Moreover, the 1906 three-nation treaty has already largely defined the spheres of influence of Britain and Italy, so at present Britain only raises the issue of the free use of the source of the Chana Lake in the upper reaches of the Nile River for negotiation, and all other issues can be resolved easily. After the three countries agree on this method in principle, Britain and Italy will probably ask France to initiate and convene a three-nation conference. The tasks of the three-nation conference are twofold: one is to determine the boundaries of the British and Italian spheres of influence in Abyssinia, and the other is to establish a new method of managing Abyssinian territory while respecting its superficial sovereignty. It is said that the British and Italian sides are very much in favor of this plan, but the British government has not yet formally expressed its consent. It is estimated that there will be a decision at today's cabinet meeting. (Havas, 10th)

Compromise Plan Not From Italy

(Paris) The "Paris Echo" reported that the compromise resolution on the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, which was circulated outside yesterday, was declared by the Italian embassy in London not to have been proposed by the Italian ambassador. The newspaper also said that "part of this plan was suggested by League of Nations Secretary-General Avenol." (Havas, 11th)

Japan Dissatisfied with Russia's Proposal for Establishing Border Commission 54

(Tokyo) When Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev met with Foreign Minister Hirota yesterday, he proposed that the handling of the Japanese-Soviet-Manchurian border be based on the agreement concluded with Romania in 1923 to conclude a treaty. His intention is to use the example of the treaty concluded by the Soviet Union with neighboring countries such as Romania, Poland, Lithuania, Estonia, Iran, Turkey, Finland, and Afghanistan to handle border disputes. However, the most representative of these is the treaty concluded with Poland in 1933. This treaty designates 50 kilometers of land on both sides of the border as a special administrative zone, which is sufficient to achieve the effect of peaceful handling of border dispute events. However, the Soviet Union has various military installations on the Soviet-Manchurian border in the Far East, so it does not cite this treaty, but only cites the simplest and most incomplete Romanian treaty. Moreover, it is questionable whether the treaty concluded between the Soviet Union and Romania is still valid today after the resumption of diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union. During yesterday's meeting, Foreign Minister Hirota questioned Ambassador Yurenev whether this treaty was still valid with Romania. Ambassador Yurenev could not answer immediately, but only answered that he would answer after investigation. It can be seen that the Soviet Union wants to use the simplest and most incomplete treaty as the basis for resolving the Japanese-Soviet-Manchurian border dispute. (Telegraphic Communication, 11th)

Austria Abolishes Decree Exiling Royal Family Passed by Federal Parliament First Step Towards Restoration 55

(Vienna) The Federal Parliament today passed a resolution by the government to abolish the law exiling the Habsburg royal family. When voting, it was unanimously approved. The Habsburg royal family was expelled from the country when Austria implemented the republic at the end of the European War. It has been sixteen years since then, and now they can safely return to their country. Baron Visnar, the leader of the Austrian legitimists, told Reuters that this is only the first step in the Habsburg restoration, and he hopes that the negotiations for the Grand Duke Otto to return to the country can be completed soon. The parliament's resolution seems to have aroused the anger of Romania, Yugoslavia, and Czechoslovakia, the Little Entente, because these two countries strongly oppose Austria's restoration. (Reuters, 10th)

If there is a war in East Africa, the Italian army can use this new chemical material to inflict great damage on the Abyssinian army. It is said that this material is mainly used in tanks. (World News Agency)

Italy Newly Cast Giant Bell Over Two Meters High and Weighing Ten Tons Dedicated to the Souls of Fallen Soldiers 57

Naples, Italy - A giant bell was supervised and built in the Bardo Metallurgical Factory, and has now been cast and transported to the city of Messeler, where it will be installed in the local Vittorio Shrine to dedicate it to the souls of the soldiers who died in the Great War. This bell is 2.9 meters high and weighs more than ten tons. Its size is one of the largest in the world. (Havas, 16th)

Supreme Court: Qualifications for President's Appointment 63

(Nanjing) Ju Zheng proposed to the Central Political Council that the Court Organization Law's qualifications for the appointment of the President of the Supreme Court, except for those concurrently held by the President of the Judicial Yuan, are limited to the following two: (1) having served as a Senior Rank Prosecutor or Judge for five years or more; (2) having served as a Senior Rank Prosecutor or Judge for three years or more, and as a Senior Rank Administrative Official for five years or more. Now that the implementation is about to begin, it seems that the restrictions are too strict, and it may be difficult to find suitable candidates. It is proposed to add a third qualification: having served as a Legislator for five years or more and made special contributions to the judiciary. The Central Political Council has approved the proposal as is and submitted it to the Legislative Yuan for review. The Legislative Yuan has approved and forwarded it to the Legislative Committee, which convened a meeting on the 11th to complete the review and submitted it to the Yuan meeting on the 12th for review. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11th)

(Tianjin) The Ma Jia Gou coal miners' strike has been settled. On the night of the 10th, the striking workers completely resumed work. The conditions for the Ma Jia Gou miners to resume work are three: (1) Wages during the strike period will be paid as usual; (2) Workers who blindly followed will not be investigated or punished; (3) Holiday periods for all commemorative days will be restored. International Business Telegram

—Reuters Special Business Report, July 11—

Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold price today was 140 shillings 8 pence, down 3 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market was stable this morning. The spot price was 31 pence 3125, and the futures price was 31 pence half, both up 1875. India and China made purchases, and trading was flat. The market situation at closing was stable.

American Silver: The Mount Re silver market opened higher today, up 75 to 155 pounds, significantly higher than the London silver price.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The pound price showed virtually no change against the dollar and gold coins. The opening price for British-American exchange was 4 yuan 9 jiao 6 fen 125, the same as yesterday's closing price for American-British. It rose 3125 in the first hour, fell 125 at noon, fell another 125 at 1 p.m., and then rose 125 at 2 p.m. to 4 yuan 9 jiao 6 fen 3125.

British-French: The opening price rose 3 pounds to 74 francs 90. It rose 1 pound in the first hour, fell 3 pounds at 1 p.m., and rose 3 pounds at 2 p.m. to 74 francs 91.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened down 9 pounds and then fell several more pounds, because the weather report continued to be good, and the Department of Agriculture's cotton production estimate was also favorable to the short side.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market, at 1 p.m. today, the October futures price was 6.25, down 1 pound.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market price plummeted today, because the American wheat production report was favorable to the short side, and the supply from Canada was also larger. At 1 p.m., the October futures price was 4 shillings 9 pence 25, down 1 pence 625.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened sharply lower, because the government's wheat production report was favorable to the short side. The telegram of the Liverpool price drop and the report of the Canadian Wheat Board selling more were also factors in the Chicago wheat market's weakness. Later, the price rose slightly. Miscellaneous grains opened down about 1 cent. Although the government's miscellaneous grain estimates were slightly favorable to the long side, they were ultimately affected by the wheat market. The climate is now improving, and after the opening, the price of miscellaneous grains rose slightly.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet at the opening and stable at noon. The trading price for October-December was 6 shillings 0625, the same as yesterday.

New York: New York rubber opened slightly lower. After the price fell, the market stabilized. Trading remained sluggish and uninteresting. Speculative interest was completely lacking.

Securities

New York: The New York securities market opened this morning, and although the market price was stable, it was uneven. Steel stocks were looser. Utility stocks opened slightly lower because the Senate ordered its utility company case examiners to insist on retaining the elimination of silver companies' provisions. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Stock Average opened up 3 pounds to 122.72, but after the first hour, all stocks trended downward and fell below yesterday's closing price. The prices are as follows:

Wan Fulin's Troops Ordered to Station in Baoding 83

The Military Department's Eight Great Divisions Will Arrive in Baoding Soon; Zhu Hongxun's Division Has Already Arrived as Ordered

Baoding Correspondence: After the Hebei Provincial Government moved to Baoding, Baoding has become the political center of the province. Therefore, the maintenance of public order in the provincial capital is very important. At the beginning of the provincial government's relocation to Baoding, in addition to Yu Xuezhong's 51st Army, the 17th Army's 2nd Division, which was originally stationed in Baoding, also assisted in maintaining the defense of the provincial capital and public order in the suburbs. Later, Yu Xuezhong was transferred to serve as the Commander of the Bandit Suppression Area in the border area of Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, and the divisions of the 51st Army were also transferred to the Fengxiang area in northern Shaanxi. At the same time, the 17th Army's 2nd Division was ordered to transfer to Xuzhou on the Jinpu Railway Line. Therefore, the defense of the provincial capital was only the responsibility of the police and security teams of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. The provincial government, considering the importance of public order in the provincial capital, in addition to telegraphing the Beiping Military Branch to transfer troops to Baoding to fill the defense, also planned to transfer 4,000 special police trained by the provincial government in the Caicun Qiangzhou area to Baoding to assist in maintaining the defense of the provincial capital. The Beiping Military Branch then transferred the 2nd Cavalry Division under Huang Xiansheng to take over the defense. After Huang's unit received the order, they sent the 1st Regiment under Zhang Naiqian to Baoding to take over the city defense, and transferred the 3rd Regiment to the Shijiazhuang Zhengding area to garrison. Personnel from the division headquarters are continuously moving here. The Military Branch replied ordering the division to be completely stationed in Shijiazhuang, and the public order in Baoding was the responsibility of the 130th Division under Zhu Hongxun of Wan Fulin's 53rd Army. At that time, the 2nd Cavalry Division only took over the defense of Baoding for three days before moving south to Shijiazhuang as ordered, and the 686th Regiment under Cong Zhaolin of the 130th Division of the 53rd Army arrived immediately after. All the city gates were taken over by the regiment. Currently, the 130th Division has been arriving since the 6th, and the division headquarters is located at the former site of the Baoding Military Academy outside the East Gate. Furthermore, the headquarters of the 53rd Army has also decided to move from the Xiyuan in Beiping to Baoding. The Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau has been entrusted to find the Baoding Xinggong (Imperial Palace) as the army headquarters. The army commander Wan Fulin and the eight great divisions of the army headquarters have sent personnel to Baoding to make arrangements. As for the 4,000 special police originally planned to be transferred from Caicun Cangzhou by the provincial government, it has been decided not to transfer them due to the large number of troops stationed in the provincial capital. The newly appointed Chairman of Hebei Province, Shang Zhen, has also transferred the 725th Regiment of the 139th Division to Baoding, stationed in the Liangjiang Guild Hall, Banmu Garden, and the Erdaowan area near the provincial government. The regimental commander Sun Dingchao has arrived in Baoding with his troops. It is rumored that this unit is specifically responsible for serving as the provincial government's guard. Furthermore, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, recently, in order to prevent bandits from taking advantage of the green yarn tents to disrupt the local area, has jointly discussed countermeasures with the Qingyuan County Government. It has been decided to assign the detective team of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau to be under the joint jurisdiction of both parties. In case of bandits, both parties can order them to be arrested at any time. Currently, this joint defense method has begun to be implemented. (July 7th)

Commander-in-Chief of the Guangxi Army, Ye Qi, Dies Tragically in a Horse Riding Accident 84

Bai Chongxi Cables Li Zongren About Ye's Death; Li Zongren Rushes Back to Guangxi from Guangdong

Guangzhou Correspondence: Ye Qi, the Commander-in-Chief of the Guangxi Army, flew to Hunan in the middle of last month. Having completed his mission by the end of the month, he flew directly to Guangzhou to report everything to Li Zongren, the Commander-in-Chief of the Guangxi Army, and others. On the fifth of this month, he took another Southwest Airlines flight back to Guangxi to report to Bai Chongxi. He arrived in Nanning on the evening of the fifth and had been working at the Guangxi Army Headquarters for several days. On the morning of the eighth, Ye Qi returned to work at the headquarters. Unexpectedly, the horse he was riding suddenly lost its composure. As soon as it left Taoyuan Road, it began to gallop wildly forward. Upon reaching the intersection of Gonghe Road, the horse stumbled and fell, throwing Ye off. His head was severely injured. Medical treatment proved ineffective, and he died within three hours. All circles in Guangxi Province mourned his passing. Bai Chongxi immediately cabled Li Zongren, stating: "To Commander-in-Chief Li Zongren of Guangzhou, and forwarded to Brothers Ji Kuan, Renmin, Yi Zhi, Xiang Ming, Huai Zhou, Mu Yao: Brother Cuiwei (Ye Qi) this morning (eighth) at 6:30 AM was riding to the headquarters from home to work. Upon reaching Xingning Road, his horse suddenly bolted and galloped to the intersection of Gonghe Road, where it stumbled, causing both horse and rider to fall. He sustained a severe head injury. Many Chinese and Western doctors were immediately called to treat him. According to the diagnosis of the surgeon, Brother Cui suffered a fracture of the medulla oblongata extending from the cerebellum. He was immediately unconscious, bleeding from his mouth and nose, which could not be stopped. Unfortunately, he passed away at 9:30 AM today. Heaven is unkind, depriving us of such a talent, truly a great loss to the Party and the nation. The grief is immeasurable. The political and military organizations have already established a funeral committee to handle all the post-mortem arrangements. I respectfully report this with tears. Bai Chongxi, bowing at noon." After receiving the telegram, Li Zongren, realizing that Ye Qi was currently traveling around various places to mediate the current situation, and shocked by the sudden news of his tragic death, urgently needed to return to Guangxi. Therefore, at 1:00 PM on the ninth, accompanied by his wife, Ms. Guo Dejie, Zhang Renmin, the Chief of Staff of the Guangxi Army's Office in Guangdong, and guards, he took a special train on the Guangsan Railway to Sanshui Hekou, and from Hekou, he transferred to the Hong Kong-Wuzhou steamboat "Jiangsu" to Wuzhou. He arrived in Wuzhou on the morning of the tenth, transferred to another boat, and went straight back to Nanning to discuss important matters with Bai Chongxi and handle Ye's funeral arrangements. Ye Qi, courtesy name Cuiwei, was from Rong County, Guangxi. He graduated from the Baoding Military Academy. In 1919, he joined the army, initially under Tang Shengzhi in the Hunan Army, serving as a staff officer. In 1925, when Tang Shengzhi participated in the Northern Expedition, Ye was ordered to enter Guangxi to discuss with Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, and Huang Shaohong about sending troops north. Guangxi sent the Seventh Army to participate. At that time, Tang Shengzhi's Hunan Army was reorganized into the Eighth Army, with Tang as the army commander and Ye Qi as the commander of the First Division of the Eighth Army. When the Revolutionary Army entered Hubei, Ye also served as the garrison commander of Wuhan. After the success of the Northern Expedition, he was promoted to commander of the Twelfth Army, but later resigned from his military post. Subsequently, Bai Chongxi returned to Guangxi and formed the Fourth Group Army, with Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi serving as the commander and deputy commander, respectively. In 1931, Ye served as the Chief of Staff of the Fourth Group Army, making many plans and earning the deep trust of Li and Bai. Now, he has died tragically at the young age of forty. (Evening of July 9th)

Nanhui: A Student Surveying Land Dies Suddenly After Drinking

Wang Shuhao, a surveying and arithmetic apprentice from the Land Bureau of this county, was twenty years old this year and from Yongjia, Zhejiang. On the evening of the ninth, he had a drinking session with four colleagues, and then they went to the public tea garden for tea. Wang felt unwell and returned to his residence to sleep. When his colleagues returned, they found Wang breathing weakly, thinking he had suddenly contracted acute cholera. They rushed him to the Public First Hospital for treatment. According to Dr. Sun Youxin's diagnosis, he was found to be poisoned by opium smoke and died. His brother in Shanghai was notified and came to the city on the tenth. Wanting to know the cause of his death, he decided not to prepare the body for burial for the time being. He hired someone overnight to go to Shanghai to invite a doctor to administer embalming injections so that his brother's body could be transported to Shanghai for examination.

Suzhou: Difficulties in Training Township Heads

The county government is organizing training for township heads and bao chiefs. Township heads are required to report to the province by the 17th for training, and bao chiefs are scheduled to begin training in Suzhou on the 19th. However, all the township heads in the urban area are unwilling to go to the province for training due to various reasons. They jointly submitted a petition to the First District Office on the eleventh, which was forwarded to the county and province, requesting urgent training. If this is not successful, they will all resign. County Magistrate Wu is quite hesitant about this matter and will go to the province tomorrow or the day after to seek instructions. As for the training of bao chiefs, although it is scheduled to begin, the bao chiefs are unable to take leave due to work reasons. Therefore, they will also submit a request for exemption from training.

Taicang: Many Inmates Die of Illness in Prisons

Since this county's prison and detention center began to hold opium offenders, the space has been small and the number of inmates large, resulting in severe overcrowding. During this season of the plum rains, the air is polluted and diseases are rampant. Over one hundred people suffer from dropsy, with pale and sallow complexions and swelling throughout their bodies. Death occurs when the swelling reaches the heart and mouth. Epidemics have also occurred one after another. In recent days, the following have died of illness: a robber named Huang Mi, an assailant named He Xiaodi, and opium offenders Yu Asong, Qu Jingui, Xu Agui, Zhu Baogui, Xu Xiaoheng, Zhu Renyuan, and Feng Ziqing, totaling seven people. The speed of death has set a new record never seen before. According to the prison's contracted Chinese medicine doctor Tan, most of the inmates are lying on cement floors, never exposed to the earth's energy or sunlight, and lack exercise, which causes the illnesses.

Wuxi: Labor-Management Dispute at Zhenxin Yarn Factory

On May 17th, a labor-management dispute occurred at the Zhenxin Yarn Factory outside the West Gate of this county, leading to a strike. After the party and government authorities made great efforts to mediate, the situation temporarily calmed down. However, the factory sued Wu Ada and others in court for assaulting employees and damaging factory machinery. The court summoned them for questioning. Yesterday, over a hundred male and female workers from the factory petitioned the county party headquarters and the county government, demanding that the factory be persuaded to withdraw the lawsuit. The party and government authorities have decided to summon Jiang Zhexian, the manager of the factory, for talks to facilitate mediation.

147 Opium Users Wanted

The County Opium Suppression Committee of this county has been carrying out the registration and rehabilitation of opium users. So far, nine batches have been completed, with four to five hundred people successfully quitting. However, it is inevitable that some of the opium users in each batch will give false statements and avoid registration. Although the county committee has repeatedly issued summonses in batches, some opium users still have unknown addresses, making summons impossible, or they are hiding and cannot be found. From the first to the ninth batch, the total number of such people is 147, including Fan Abao. Yesterday, the county committee instructed the Public Security Bureau to issue a unified wanted notice to all branch bureaus and offices.

Huaian: County Magistrate Reports County Affairs to the Provincial Government

As soon as County Magistrate Yao Chongguo arrived, he immediately considered the Huai River diversion project to be of utmost importance. He personally went to the construction site to supervise the work and strictly ordered the workers in each district to accelerate their work. The first phase of the project is more than two-thirds complete. After returning to the city, he convened a joint defense meeting as the summer flood season approached, determined the defense zones, and issued notices for compliance. He also led the security team to suppress bandits in the countryside, causing the bandits to flee at the mere sound of their approach. One well-known bandit was captured and another was killed. Local areas have thus found peace. Regarding opium suppression, past measures were deemed inadequate, with many unregistered opium users. Therefore, after discussions by the committee, a modified method was decided upon and submitted for approval. The baojia system is also being emphasized. The first, second, and third phases of township heads have gone to Pu for training, and baojia chiefs have been trained and completed by the district offices. Together with the security team, they conduct spot checks of households and inspect county affairs late at night. The various measures have greatly improved the situation compared to the past. Local people have praised the efforts. With outstanding achievements, County Magistrate Yao has already drafted a plan for the implementation of the 24th-year administrative policy. He requested leave on the 7th of this month to go to the province to report on the recent administrative situation and to seek instructions on all future administrative policies. All daily government affairs are temporarily being handled by Secretary Li Yusong.

Loan Review Committee Sends Letter Urging Approval of Loan Regulations 85

Since the establishment of the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee and its active operation, it has drafted loan regulations and other documents and submitted them to the Ministry of Finance for approval and promulgation. Due to the high expectations from all parties, a letter has been sent urging a response. Application forms for loans have also been drafted and will soon be distributed for completion and submission for review. The details are as follows:

Letter Urging Approval of Loan Regulations

Cai Zengji, the chairman of the Loan Review Committee, sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance yesterday stating: "The circumstances of the establishment of this committee, as well as the draft articles of association, operating procedures, and detailed rules for Shanghai industry and commerce guaranteed loans, were reported to your ministry on June 26 for review and approval. Only after the aforementioned articles and rules are approved and promulgated by your ministry can all the affairs of this committee be handled accordingly. At present, industries and businesses in this city are eagerly awaiting the implementation of loans, like a severe drought longing for rain clouds. Those who come to the committee every day to inquire and request are endless. Some even blame the slow progress due to excessive expectations, which shows that the economic situation in the city is deteriorating day by day, and rescue cannot be delayed any longer. However, the previous request for approval of the articles and rules has not yet received a reply, and all affairs cannot be started. This committee witnesses the difficulties and deeply understands the heavy responsibility. Non-members of trade associations can also obtain application forms from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and submit them for review. As for the mortgage loan application forms, they will likely be submitted to various lending banks (such as the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, etc.) for applicants to fill out. All applications that have been reviewed and qualified by the committee in accordance with the articles and rules can be granted loans.

China-Philippines Trade Association Representatives Go to Beijing to Petition for Assistance in Trade with the Philippines 86

There are approximately 50,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines, most of whom are engaged in business in the Philippines. The sale of domestic goods in the Philippines has been very developed in the past, often dominating the Philippine market. Recently, neighboring countries have been selling low-priced goods in the Philippines, causing the sales of Chinese goods in the Philippine market to plummet. If no immediate measures are taken to save the situation, the livelihood of more than 50,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines will be cut off. The reasons for the failure of Chinese goods in the Philippines include the heavy blow from the dumping of goods by neighboring countries, but the trend of decline should also include the following points: (1) Exchange rate impact, (2) High tariffs, (3) Excessive freight, resulting in excessively high costs, making it impossible to compete with others. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and overseas Chinese in the Philippines jointly formed the China-Philippines Trade Promotion Association to address the decline of Chinese goods in the Philippines, plan future strategies to promote trade with the Philippines, and send representatives Ding Hongxiang and Chen Cailiang to Beijing to request guidance and assistance from the government to develop trade with the Philippines, rescue overseas Chinese in the Philippines, and take the opportunity to promote the external sales of domestic products.

It Is Difficult to Achieve Salary Reduction in the Shipping Industry A Ship Crew Strike Is Expected to Subside 90

The various shipping companies within the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association previously discussed reducing the salaries of ship crews from July 1st, which triggered strong opposition from the three groups of marine engineers, navigators, and radio operators, as well as thirteen groups including marine engineers, navigators, and sailors from Nanshi, almost leading to a major strike. Now that this matter is about to disappear invisibly, it is of great concern to the shipping industry. Details are as follows:

Softening Attitude of Sanbei

Sanbei Company first reduced the salaries of ship crews to 80% from July 1st, with a uniform discount for those earning more than 50 yuan. All the ship crews requested that Yu Qiaqing exempt them from the reduction. Yu initially refused, but after the ship crews requested that the back pay be paid first and then discuss the salary reduction, Sanbei Company could not help but hesitate. Therefore, its response to the three groups of marine engineers, navigators, and radio operators was that the salary reduction matter is currently being negotiated with the ship crews and a satisfactory solution that both parties can understand is expected.

Other Declarations of No Reduction

Since the three groups of ship crews issued a notice limiting each shipping company to clearly state its attitude on whether to reduce salaries within three days, companies that are not members of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, such as Dalu Company and Antong Company, have formally sent letters to the marine engineers, navigators, and radio operators stating that since they are not members of the association, there will be no salary reduction and the original amount will still be paid. Other companies, such as Datong and Dada, have also verbally notified that they will not reduce the salaries of ship crews. Ning Shao Company said that if other companies do not reduce, they will follow suit. All the shipping companies, in view of the problems arising from the salary reduction matter, are all silent and dare not issue any more salary reduction notices.

Resumption of Salaries for Dazhen Ship Crews

Due to the suspension of navigation of the Dazhen Shipping Company's Yongping and Yongan vessels, the ship crews have been receiving 60% of their salaries for a long time. After the issue of salary reduction arose, the ship crews of the two vessels have requested the company authorities to restore the full salary from July 1st. If they continue to receive 60% of their salaries, it would be similar to a salary reduction, which may cause misunderstandings by other companies and difficulties for both ship crews and shipping companies. Negotiations are currently underway.

Impact on China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Ship Crews

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is not a member of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association and has always taken an independent stance on ship crew salaries. After the ship crews of the company requested a salary increase, after a long period of negotiation, the chief masters of the ship department revised the new salary increase regulations, dividing them into three grades: A, B, and C, and obtained the approval of the board of directors. It was submitted to the Ministry of Communications for approval and was originally scheduled to be implemented on July 1st. Unexpectedly, the salary reduction issue arose, and the Ministry of Communications did not immediately approve this case, resulting in failure to implement it on July 1st, which affected the ship crews.

Hardware and Lumber Industries Suspend Ordering Foreign Goods for Three Months The National Tariff Commission Announces That Foreign Goods Will Not Be Ordered From This Month 92

China News Agency: The National Tariff Commission announced yesterday the wholesale price index: The wholesale price index, with a general index of 92.1, fell by 2.2% compared to the previous month and 3.8% compared to the same month last year. Compared with the previous month, all category indexes fell except for a slight increase in chemicals. The five categories of food, other foods, metals, building materials, and textiles showed the sharpest declines. The food category fell by 6.2%. Although Su Tong rice and Min Dang rice rose due to drought and shortage, wheat, flour, soybeans, and other grains tended to fall due to the arrival of new goods or price declines in the producing areas. The other foods category fell by 2.3%. Although green tea exports are not bad, the market price still fell sharply in line with black tea. The price of new goods was much higher than that of old goods when the new season goods were released in May. It is expected that prices will gradually fall back, as in previous years. In addition, raw peanuts fell due to the decline of Cantonese tongs, sesame oil fell due to sluggish sales, and coarse sugar, white sugar, American tobacco leaves, fresh oranges, pork, ham, protein, salted fish, etc. also weakened. Both the metals and building materials categories fell by 3.1%. The indexes of these two categories have been declining in recent months. The Hardware and Lumber Industries Association decided that from July, members will not order goods from abroad for three months, which proves the sluggish sales and abundant inventory. Textiles fell by 3.0%. The cotton yarn and cotton cloth market was quiet due to tight money, and foreign goods were strongly competing in China, further impacting actual sales. All the yarn factories have stopped their machines and reduced their working hours, which resulted in decreased demand for cotton, causing the prices of cotton, yarn, and cloth to fall uniformly. White silk also fell due to sluggish exports.

The Ministry of Finance Yesterday Again Sternly Ordered Ning Shi to Expedite the Return of Savings Deposits; Deadline Expired, No Further Extension Allowed 93

After the Ningbo Industrial Bank suspended operations on the 4th of last month, the Ministry of Finance immediately ordered the bank the next day to fully repay all savings deposits within one month of receiving the order. That deadline has now passed, but the bank has not complied. The Ministry of Finance previously ordered the bank to settle the matter within ten days. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance again ordered the bank to expedite the return of savings deposits, and also instructed Luo Zongmeng, the supervisor and liquidator, to relay this message to the bank's directors and supervisors. The original text of the instructions is compiled as follows:

Ministry of Finance Order to Ning Wen: The Ministry of Finance yesterday issued another order to the Ningbo Industrial Bank, stating that the bank had announced its suspension of operations and liquidation. The Ministry had already ordered on June 5th of this year to immediately return savings deposits and to fully repay them within one month of receiving the order. If the bank's assets were insufficient to repay depositors' savings, the bank's directors and supervisors should bear joint and unlimited liability for repayment according to law, without fail. It has been found that the deadline has expired, and it has not been reported that the savings deposits received have begun to be returned, which is a disregard for the law and harms the interests of depositors. This is unacceptable. Therefore, this order is issued to urge immediate and strict compliance with repeated Ministry orders, to expedite the full return of all savings deposits as a priority, and to avoid intentional delays that would lead to strict investigation. Other debts should also be settled promptly to ensure an early conclusion. This is of utmost importance. This order is imperative.

Order to Supervisor and Liquidator: At the same time, the Ministry of Finance also issued an order to Luo Zongmeng, the supervisor and liquidator of the Ningbo Industrial Bank, stating that the Ningbo Industrial Bank had announced its suspension of operations and liquidation. The Ministry had already ordered on June 5th of this year to immediately return savings deposits and to fully repay them within one month of receiving the order. If the bank's assets were insufficient to repay depositors' savings, the bank's directors and supervisors should bear joint and unlimited liability for repayment according to law, without fail. It has been found that the deadline has expired, and it has not been reported that the savings deposits received have begun to be returned, which is a disregard for the law and harms the interests of depositors. This is completely unacceptable. In addition to ordering the bank to strictly comply with repeated Ministry orders, to expedite the full return of all savings deposits as a priority, and to avoid intentional delays that would lead to strict investigation, and to promptly settle other debts to ensure an early conclusion, this order is also issued for your information. This order.

Regarding the Case of Ning Shi Directors and Supervisors: Luo Zongmeng, the special commissioner appointed by the Ministry of Finance to supervise the liquidation of Ning Shi, also sent a letter to all Ning Shi directors and supervisors yesterday morning, urging them to expedite the liquidation. The original text reads: Sirs, regarding the liquidation of the Ningbo Industrial Bank, the Board of Directors of your bank and the relevant personnel were previously notified via letters on June 13th and 23rd to select liquidators and handle the bank's liquidation affairs within a specified period. One month has passed since then, but your bank has neither convened a shareholders' meeting nor selected liquidators. The directors and supervisors have either made excuses to shirk responsibility or have absconded, clearly infringing upon the rights of depositors. To protect the rights and interests of creditors, this commissioner has reported this to the Ministry of Finance for review. Now, Instruction No. 159016 from the Ministry of Finance states, "The report and attachments have been duly noted. In addition to issuing orders for compliance, it has been found that the bank has been suspended operations for almost a month and has neither convened an extraordinary shareholders' meeting to make resolutions according to law nor appointed liquidators to be responsible for liquidation. This prolonged delay not only hinders the interests of creditors but also violates orders, which is completely unacceptable. Previously, Supervisor and Liquidator Luo Zongmeng's report requesting a thorough review was not received by the Ministry. You are hereby urgently ordered to select liquidators and commence liquidation within ten days of receiving this document. If liquidators are still not selected by the deadline, the bank's directors will act as liquidators to handle liquidation affairs to ensure an early conclusion. Furthermore, it has been found that the bank also operates savings business. According to the Savings Bank Law and the approved regulations of the bank's savings department, directors, supervisors, and managers bear joint and several liability for repayment. The regulations are very strict and should be followed. You are urged to comply with previous Ministry orders and repay savings deposits and other debts within the specified period. If you continue to evade or delay, the Ministry will definitely pursue the matter strictly in accordance with the law, without leniency. This order is imperative." In addition to instructing the Ningbo Industrial Bank to comply, you are also hereby notified to comply with previous Ministry orders, earnestly supervise the liquidation, and report the bank's financial situation in detail. Attachments are enclosed. This order, etc. Having received this order, it should be complied with accordingly. It has been found that your bank also operates savings business. According to Articles 12 and 15 of the Savings Bank Law promulgated by the National Government on July 4, 1934, during the period when your directors and supervisors' legal duties are not fulfilled, you cannot arbitrarily shirk responsibility. Therefore, it is your duty to comply with the Ministry's order within the specified period, convene an extraordinary shareholders' meeting, select liquidators, and expedite the liquidation to avoid any inconvenience. Regarding the aforementioned orders, in addition to complying with the orders to earnestly supervise the liquidation to protect the rights and interests of creditors, we are also sending you the attendance records of the two sessions of the Board of Directors and Supervisors for your reference and action. This is addressed to the Directors and Supervisors of the Ningbo Industrial Bank. From Luo Zongmeng, Special Commissioner Appointed by the Ministry of Finance to Supervise the Liquidation of the Ningbo Industrial Bank.

Gospel for Patients with Kala-azar: Save Three Lives with Two Yuan: Donate to the Chinese and Foreign Relief Society 102

Since kala-azar (a Chinese medicine name is "Pi Kuai Disease", and the Western medicine name is "kala-azar") has occurred in the counties north of the Yangtze River, the speed of its spread and the number of deaths are more terrifying than floods and fierce beasts. It is indeed alarming. Anyone who is infected is as good as being sentenced to death. Not only is it spreading more and more widely and fiercely, but it also has a significant impact on the people's livelihood and the nation. Recently, Mr. Wang Shuxiang, a gentleman from Huaiyin, came to Shanghai and said that there is an ancient Chinese medicine prescription that has a miraculous effect in treating this disease. It has been reported in the previous newspapers. After philanthropists visited Mr. Wang at his inn and asked for his prescription, Mr. Wang verbally stated that Zuisheng Jun, seeing righteousness and acting bravely, donated 100 yuan of medicine funds and sent it to the Chinese and Foreign Relief Society. There are also many other enthusiastic people who are happy to help, and concerned people from all walks of life have also sent letters to inquire in detail. Because it is too late to return home to reply to them one by one, since you have inquired, I am willing to make the prescription public to all those who are destined. (The prescription is below) According to the prescription, the cost of medicine is only two yuan, which can save three lives. Compared with the value of Western medicine, it is less than one-fifteenth. However, the medicine refining procedures are complicated and must not be mistaken. It is only limited to treating this disease. Although there is a universal desire for compassion, it is limited by the strength of cotton, and there are too many people infected with this disease, which requires a huge expense. The area north of the Yangtze River has always been known for its poverty, and it is difficult to raise funds. If there are those who make this good wish and donate medicine funds, because I am away from Shanghai, you can send this money directly to the Chinese and Foreign Relief Society at No. 97 Renji Road in this port for collection, so as to expand the relief.

(A) Kala-azar Pill Prescription (This cannot be taken if you are not sick) Two liang of alum (must be calcined twice before use), one catty of soybean flour, four liang of woodlice, four liang of black dates, eight liang of angelica, eight liang of brown sugar. This is one dose, grind into extremely fine powder, and make into pills with rice soup and honey. Each pill weighs three fen. Take seven pills three times a day, morning, noon, and evening, before meals, with goose saliva water. Increase the amount according to the proportion. However, the alum must be put into a silver mud pot and refined into vermilion in a large furnace fire before taking it out. After cooling, refine it again. This must be done three times before it can be used. It is most important. Also, the wine prescription is one catty of old yellow wine, two liang of chicken gizzard skin, four liang of woodlice, one liang of angelica, and one qian of safflower. The above five ingredients should be buried in the soil for one hundred days before they can be taken out. Take five qian each time, one or two hours after taking the pills. Drink it, increase the amount according to the proportion. (B) Kala-azar Plaster Prescription, sapling root, kelp, mirabilite, purple millet, castor seeds, purple sesame seeds, and Sichuan lovage, equal parts of the seven flavors, forty-eight liang in total, boil into plaster, each piece weighs three qian, add asafoetida, one-tenth of the previous medicine.

Dutch Giant Wheel Steams to South Africa Yesterday Morning 104

The Houtman, a Dutch Royal Mail Line ship sailing on the Asia-Africa long-distance route, arrived in Shanghai on the 5th from East Africa. Because the ship's engine was damaged, it entered the dock for repairs. The work has now been completed, so it sailed from Shanghai to various ports in South Africa yesterday morning. Along the way, it will pass through Cebu, Manila, Saigon, Bangkok, Singapore, Batavia, Mauritius, Lourenço Marques, Beira, East London, Port Elizabeth, Mozambique Channel, Cape of Good Hope, and then return from the Cape of Good Hope to Beira, Datiemawei, Liverpool, Mauritius, Lourenço Marques, Batavia, Singapore, Cebu, Hong Kong, and other places.

Tramcar Industry Actively Prepares Mutual Aid Association; Car Households Registered Have Reached More Than 5,600; Field Car Donation Increased, Car Households Demand Contact and Oppose 106

The tramcar industry in this city has caused a reaction from the tramcar industry in the city due to the resolution of the Public Concession Industry Bureau's tramcar office to increase tramcar donations in the autumn. The air of demanding restrictions from the Chinese tax-paying associations and all walks of life in the concession has been very tense in recent days. In order to seek mutual assistance and contact, the people in this industry have also initiated the organization of the Shanghai Tramcar Industry Mutual Aid Association, intending to develop and prepare for it. Since the preparations began, they have been actively carrying out their work without leaving any effort. The number of tramcar households in the city who have applied to the preparatory office of the association for membership has also been very enthusiastic. As of yesterday, it is heard that there were more than 5,600 households. The preparatory office of the association is deeply concerned that there may be omissions because the scope of the city is quite wide and the same industry is scattered in various directions. Therefore, it has specially sent letters to each car household to universally solicit members. Its notification says: Greetings. It has been found that the Public Concession Tramcar Office has suddenly resolved to increase tramcar donations to as much as one time, regardless of the difficult times, which is extremely destructive to hard work. In order to maintain life in today's sluggish market and declining business, in addition to separately requesting the Chinese tax-paying associations in the concession and the Nantong Fellow Association in Shanghai to ask the Labor Bureau on behalf of them to withdraw their orders and stop increasing donations, in order to promote the overall development of our industry and to encourage mutual contact and emotions, we have also organized the Shanghai Tramcar Industry Mutual Aid Association. Since the initiation of preparations, the number of car households who have come to the association to apply for membership has been very enthusiastic. However, the scope of the city is quite wide, and the same industry is scattered in various directions. We are deeply concerned that there may be omissions. Therefore, we have sent another notification to all of you, asking you to quickly come to the association to register in the spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation. This matter is closely related to your personal interests, so please do not wait and see. This is addressed to all car households. The office of this association is located at No. 4 Yongji Li, at the intersection of Xizang Road and Avenue Edward VII, attached to the Nantong Fellow Association in Shanghai due to economic reasons.

In other news, the Public Concession Tramcar Office has recently increased the donation for collapsed cars, causing the collapsed car households in the city to panic. Yesterday, they specially sent representatives to the preparatory office of the Tramcar Industry Mutual Aid Association to request contact and unanimously opposed it.

Regulations of the Railway Department on Compensation for Lost Joint Transportation Luggage; Yesterday's Order to the Two Railway Bureaus for Compliance 109

The Two Railway Bureaus yesterday received an order from the Railway Department stating that, according to a case presented by the Business Department, the 162nd proposal of the 9th National Railway Transportation Conference concerned the lack of a market price to determine the compensation amount for lost luggage transported by freight cars and the difficulty in verifying the value declared on the consignment note. It proposed that compensation standards be established. The 130th resolution of the conference resolved to handle it according to the compensation value stipulated in the passenger car transportation regulations, and to note it in the cargo classification table. Upon review, this was deemed feasible and approved for implementation. In addition to noting in the baggage section (personal belongings) of the 30th category of the classification table (if there is compensation for loss, the limit of compensation price shall be handled in accordance with Article 71 of the passenger car transportation regulations) and issuing separate orders, the Two Railway Bureaus are hereby ordered to comply. This order includes the text of Article 71 of the passenger car transportation regulations: "For luggage handed over to the railway for transportation or storage, if there is any loss or damage due to the railway's fault, the railway shall be responsible for compensation according to the verified value. However, the maximum limit shall be as follows: (A) Suitcases, leather bags, or boxes: up to 100 yuan per piece; (B) Bedding: up to 30 yuan per bundle; (C) Baskets: up to 10 yuan per piece, and the railway is not responsible for any loss of items inside the basket. For insured luggage, compensation shall be made according to the insured amount in case of loss, except for natural disasters or force majeure events that cannot be resisted by human power. If there is damage, compensation shall be made according to the verified extent of damage, with the maximum still limited to the insured amount."

Two Railway Bureaus and Xin Yun Company Signed a Joint Passenger and Freight Transportation Contract; Effective August 1st for a Term of One Year 110

For the convenience of passenger and freight transportation in Jiangbei, the Two Railway Bureaus, after consultation with Xin Yun Steamship Company (formerly Fu Yun Company), which operates between Qingjiangpu and Zhenjiang, have negotiated and finalized a joint water-land transportation contract for passenger luggage, parcels, and freight. The Traffic Department has submitted it to the Bureau for formal signing, and it is scheduled to take effect on August 1st for a term of one year. The full text is excerpted as follows:

Article 1 of the joint water-land transportation states that the Railway Bureau and the Company shall handle joint transportation of passenger luggage, parcels, and freight in accordance with the provisions of this contract. All current regulations and detailed rules for passenger and freight transportation that do not conflict with this contract shall apply to this joint transportation within their respective jurisdictions. Article 2 states that the Railway Bureau designates Nanjing, Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, Shangbei, Shangnan, and Maigen Road as responsible freight transportation stations, and the Company designates Shaobo, Gaoyou, Baoying, Huaicheng, Qingjiang, Taixian, and Liubu as passenger and freight connecting stations. Other stations and ports may be expanded upon mutual agreement when needed. Article 3 states that the freight charges for joint water-land transportation shall be calculated by adding the current freight rates for the distances traveled by both parties, based on kilograms, metric tons, and meters as the standard of calculation, and shall be collected in cash only. All goods with reduced fees, free of charge, or on account shall not be jointly transported. Joint transportation passenger fares shall be jointly determined according to the prices due to both parties. A detailed price list for joint transportation passenger tickets shall be provided separately, which shall also form part of this contract. If either party wishes to modify any freight rates in the future, it must notify the other party with sufficient advance notice. Article 4 states that the revenue from joint transportation business shall be reported by both parties in lists every ten days and settled monthly. The monthly joint transportation reports shall be exchanged by both parties before the 15th of the following month for detailed verification. The Railway Bureau shall then prepare a settlement statement and notify the Civil Affairs Bureau for clear delivery before the 25th of the same month. Article 5 states that the revenue from joint water-land passenger and freight transportation shall be designated by the Railway Bureau and the Company respectively, with reputable banks approved by the relevant parties responsible for guaranteeing and collecting and paying on schedule without delay.

Article 6 of passenger and freight transportation states that, when necessary for the transportation of large numbers of passengers or goods, the originating party shall notify the relevant parties by advance telegram to prepare for connection. Article 7 states that the destination station or port shall be responsible for checking and processing the freight, luggage, or parcel tickets for joint water-land transportation. If there is an error and the destination station or port fails to detect it, if the amount is short-collected and the consignee or consignor fails to pay the shortfall, and it is impossible to recover it, then the shortfall shall be borne equally by the originating and destination Railway Bureau or Company. If there is an overcollection and it is impossible to refund it, the overcollection shall be divided equally between the originating and destination Railway Bureau or Company. Article 8 states that the format of joint water-land passenger tickets and documents shall be in accordance with railway regulations for uniformity. If there is a need for changes, they shall be discussed and agreed upon by both the Railway Bureau and the Company. These passenger tickets and documents shall be printed and issued by the Railway Bureau. The Railway Bureau shall bear the printing costs for those used by the Railway Bureau, and the Company shall bear the printing costs for those used by the Company (however, for various documents that are required by the Railway Bureau alone and the Company is requested to fill out, the blank documents shall be provided by the Railway Bureau). For various stamps required for joint transportation, both parties shall determine the style and engrave them separately for their own use. Article 9 states that the costs of joint promotional materials for joint water-land transportation shall be shared equally by both parties. Other costs belonging to one party shall be borne by that party. Promotional materials shall also be sent to each other at any time for application. Article 10 states that the Company may send unencrypted telegrams or use telephones free of charge at each joint transportation station for official business related to joint transportation, but it must be approved and signed by the stationmaster.

Article 11 on Company commissions states that the Railway Bureau shall pay the Company a commission based on the total net revenue earned by the Railway Bureau from the Company's monthly joint passenger and freight transportation revenue. For each month less than 5,000 yuan, a commission of 1.5% shall be paid. For revenue above 5,000 yuan, a commission of 3% shall be paid. However, joint passenger and freight revenue from shipments sold by the Railway Bureau shall not be subject to commission. Article 12 states that the detailed rules for joint water-land passenger and freight transportation shall be discussed separately and form part of this contract. Article 13 states that the benefits stipulated in this contract may not be transferred without the written consent of the Railway Bureau. In case of violation, the Railway Bureau may cancel the contract. Article 14 states that the effective period of this contract shall be from August 1, 1935 to July 31, 1936, tentatively set for one year. Both parties shall notify each other one month before the expiration of the contract as to whether or not to continue it. If the contract is terminated upon expiration, the joint transportation matters occurring within the validity period of the contract shall continue to be handled and enjoy various rights. Article 15 states that any matters not covered by this contract may be notified in writing at any time and revised by both parties through consultation. Article 16 states that this contract is signed in duplicate original, with each party holding one copy as evidence of good faith. Another copy is kept by the Railway Bureau for record.

Regarding the store strike in the Baoxingli area, the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, upon resolution of the representative assembly, sent Chen Jiufeng, Zhang Xianfang, Zheng Xiaolin, Wang Jingdong, Wang Xianjue, Zheng Jianbo, and six other representatives to negotiate with the landlord Tongfu Company yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. The company representative agreed to convey this intention to the shareholders' meeting for a decision. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the six representatives went to the Public Security Bureau to petition. The Public Security Bureau stated that the members of the association were complex and the organization was illegal. They had inquired with the Municipal Party Department and the Social Bureau, and the reply was that it had not been registered. Moreover, since the association had not been closed down, the strike by the merchants was considered meddling. Jin Zhongjian of the Second Section only received them in a personal capacity, advising them to quell the situation and bring peace, but without result, they returned.

Robbery of Collector at Hongchang Money Exchange; Fierce Gunfight with Police; Two Robbers Fled in Panic but Ultimately Captured; Robber Opens Fire, Wounding Officer and Bystander in Hot Pursuit 116

At around 3:00 PM yesterday, Hongchang Money Exchange at No. 413 Sichuan Road instructed Liu Yuqing, a 24-year-old runner from Ba County, to collect over 7,000 yuan in outstanding debts from a rice shop at the intersection of Changan Road and Guangfu Road in Zhabei. Liu immediately hired a rickshaw, instructing the driver, Yong Caifu, to pull him to Zhabei. A total of 7,000 yuan in cash was collected, divided into two bundles: one of 5,000 yuan and one of 2,000 yuan. Unexpectedly, Liu's movements had been noticed by bandits. As Liu prepared to return to the Exchange, his rickshaw was stopped by four or five bandits next to New Zha Road, near the New Zha Bridge; one of the bandits had a gun. They ordered Liu to get out of the rickshaw, forcibly dragged him into a nearby dark alley called Yongshou Lane, and demanded that he hand over the banknotes. Knowing he had encountered robbers, Liu desperately clutched the two bundles of banknotes tightly. Seeing that Liu refused to comply, the bandits joined forces to seize the bundle of 5,000 yuan in cash and fled out of the lane. Liu Yuqing gave chase, but it was too late. He only saw two robbers crossing New Zha Bridge and escaping towards Wuzhen Road in the Chinese district. Liu's rickshaw driver was very alert. Knowing that his master had met with trouble, he rushed to the Huafu police station near the New Zha Bridge to report the incident, indicating that the two people running ahead were the robbers. Upon receiving the report, the patrol officer frantically blew his whistle and chased after them towards the north side of the bridge. Upon hearing this, the two robbers turned towards the vicinity of the Wuzhen Road police station. The police officers at the Wuzhen Road police station were already guarding the area. Seeing two men in short clothes running desperately, they immediately ordered them to stop. The robber in the lead, seeing that the police officers had surrounded them on all sides and knowing it was difficult to escape, immediately surrendered. The robber behind, seeing his path blocked, turned back towards Gonghe Road to escape. Upon seeing this, police chief Hu Yao and police officer Hu Kuitao from the police station urgently chased after him with guns. Seeing that the pursuit was pressing, the robber turned again towards Manchuria Road and ran towards Mongolia Road. At the Guoging Road intersection, he encountered police officer Li Zhaokui, No. 2303, from post No. 21 on Wuzhen Road, a native of Beiping, who was on duty. Witnessing the scene, he also drew his gun and assisted in the pursuit. At that time, police officer Li, regardless of his own safety, jumped ahead and relentlessly chased after him. Seeing that the distance was not far and fearing capture, the robber, in a moment of desperation, turned back and opened fire, firing three shots in a row. Police officer Li was unable to dodge in time and was shot in the right foot, collapsing to the ground in extreme pain. The robber continued to run forward. When he reached the Gongxing Small Vegetable Market, other police officers had arrived from all directions and were surrounding the robber in the center. Knowing he could no longer resist, the robber was captured. A pistol, No. 48075, was also seized, and 1,000 yuan in stolen cash was found on his person. He was taken to the police station. He confessed that his name was Yu Chuntao, a native of Gaoyou, 24 years old. The robber previously captured was named Zou Shuigen, a native of Suzhou, 27 years old. The remaining 4,000 yuan in stolen cash had been divided among accomplices who had escaped. After the police station obtained the confession, they immediately instructed detectives to continue the pursuit. The two captured robbers are being detained temporarily and will be handed over for legal proceedings. Police officer Li Zhaokui, who was injured in the line of duty, was sent to the hospital for treatment. As the injury was not critical, it was not expected to be life-threatening. A detailed report of the incident has been prepared and submitted to the General Bureau for review. At the same time, a bystander, whose name is unknown, was grazed by a stray bullet when the police and robbers exchanged fire and was sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment.

Thunderstorm in the City Yesterday 117

The city has been exceptionally hot for the past three days. The Fahrenheit thermometer suddenly rose to 95 or 96 degrees, setting a new record for the highest temperature this year. Consequently, the poor people living on the second, third, and even attic floors, as well as in the grass sheds in Jiangbei, were unable to sleep well at night and were sleeping on rooftops or in alleyways. Street vendors selling Dutch water, steam water, and other cold items saw their profits triple in a short time. Three days ago, a load of watermelons (about 250-260 catties) at the New Zha Bridge, Old Zha Bridge, and 16 Pu areas of the South City sold for one yuan and there were no buyers. Now, the price per load has increased to about ten yuan. The weather was particularly stuffy starting yesterday morning, with dense clouds in the sky. Although there were brief glimpses of sunlight, they were intermittent. After 1:00 PM, thunder rumbled incessantly and violently. At 1:30 PM, light rain began, followed by heavy raindrops like a downpour. However, the raindrops stopped in less than a quarter of an hour. After 3:00 PM, the clouds dispersed, the sky cleared, and the scorching sun made it unbearable. Although walking in the streets felt relatively cool, the stuffiness indoors was even worse.

Joint Office of Domestic Match Industry Officially Opens Yesterday; Branch Offices in Various Locations Begin Operations on the Same Day; Newly Established Joint Public Price Implemented Yesterday 118

According to Datong News Agency, the domestic match industry in this city, in order to unify production and sales cooperation, organized a Joint Office of Domestic Match Industry, which was established on the 1st of this month and officially started operations yesterday.

List of Directors of the Joint Office

The eight match factories in the four provinces that have joined the joint office in this city for joint operations include Da Zhonghua, Zhongguo, Zhengda, Tong Sui, Daming, Minsheng, Huai Shang, and Dahua. A board of directors consisting of eleven members was first established, with members mutually recommended by each factory. The list is recorded as follows: Liu Hongsheng, Xu Zhiyi, Lin Zhaotang, Lu Zhaolin, He Shichang, Xi Jianqing, Shao Xiuwu (the above seven also serve as executive directors), Chen Juru, Wang Jianyan, Sun Runzhai, Gao Songfu.

Appointments of Heads of Departments Determined

The office organization, in addition to the director and deputy director, also includes three departments: business, general affairs, and accounting. Chen Juru is the director, Sun Runzhai is the deputy director, Wang Jianyan is the head of the business department, Wu Weihou is the deputy, Dong Zhaoling is the head of the general affairs department, Gao Songfu is the deputy, Ye Zanqing is the head of the accounting department, and Liu Wuqi is the deputy. Branch offices are established in fourteen ports outside the city, with one director assigned to each to handle affairs. The names of the locations and the appointed directors are as follows: Zhenjiang Cao Suishan, Nanjing Ba Xingbo, Wuhu Chen Shunyu, Jiujiang Shen Liangsi, Nanchang Ke Xinzhai, Changsha Chen Defen, Ningbo Xu Ri, Nantong Xi Zemin, Suzhou Wang Shouyi, Hangzhou Zhang Zhonghui, Linhuai Wu Yihua, Fuzhou Shen Songde, Xiamen Hua Futang. There is also a location in Hankou, but the appointment has not yet been determined.

Officially Began Operations Yesterday

The office in this city is located on the fifth floor of the Enterprise Bank at No. 33 Sichuan Road, and officially started operations yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. The branch offices in various locations were also organized and established separately on the 1st of this month, and all started operations at the same time yesterday. From yesterday onwards, the operations of the eight match companies that have joined the office will be managed by the office. The matches produced by each factory are divided into three grades, and a unified price list has been established, which will also be implemented from yesterday.
