Maoli New Ship Makes Maiden Voyage on Shanghai-Taiwan Route; Reception and Viewing Held Yesterday, Departure That Evening 119

The Maoli Shipping Bureau's new ship, Maoli No. 2, has been completed by the Qiuxin Shipyard. A reception for viewing by people from all walks of life was held yesterday before its maiden voyage on the Shanghai-Taiwan route. It will travel back and forth every seven days thereafter. The details are as follows:

Completed Construction

The Maoli Wheel of the Bureau has a total tonnage of 805 tons and a net tonnage of 494 tons. The new ship Maoli No. 2 has a total tonnage of 1,134 tons and a net tonnage of 661 tons. The ship is 19.5 zhang long and 3 zhang wide, with a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour. The hull was purchased and built by the French-owned Qiuxin Shipyard in this city, and the construction has been completed. The construction cost is about 130,000 yuan in national currency. The test drive was held the day before yesterday, and the results were excellent. The interior layout has also been completed. Yesterday, it docked at Pier 11 in Nanshi, welcoming people from all walks of life to board and visit. The Bureau sent special personnel to receive guests on board. At 5:00 PM, it made its maiden voyage from Shanghai to Huangyan, passing through ports such as Dinghai, Putuo, Shipu, and Haimen.

Announcement of Sailing

The General Bureau announced, "To develop China's shipping industry and facilitate passenger and cargo transport between Shanghai and Taiwan, the original Maoli Wheel has been well-received since it began operating on the Shanghai-Taiwan route. Recently, due to insufficient cabin and tonnage, we have invested heavily in ordering a Maoli No. 2 double-bottomed fast ship from overseas. The hull is solid, the voyage is stable and fast, and it is equipped with Western-style bathtubs, hot and cold water, sand filter tanks, and hygienic lower class cabins with heat protection equipment, which is especially special. It is also equipped with multiple radios and radios to listen to broadcasts from various places to eliminate passenger loneliness. The tea room service is particularly attentive, and the loading and unloading of goods is particularly simple. The ship docks at Pier 11 in Nanshi and will depart from Shanghai to Dinghai, Putuo, Shipu, Haimen, and Huangyan on July 11. On Mondays, it will depart from Huangyan Haimen and return to Shanghai. It will travel back and forth every seven days thereafter. This is a further announcement."

Fire at Gonghe Cinema on Fangbang Bridge in Ximen; Entire Building Destroyed with Significant Losses; Tram Traffic Interrupted for Approximately Half an Hour 120

The Gonghe Cinema, located at No. 160 Minguo Road, Fangbang Bridge, Ximen, Nanshi, suddenly caught fire at around 5:50 PM yesterday. The entire building was destroyed, and it took an hour to extinguish the fire. When the fire was raging, traffic along Minguo Road in that area was interrupted for approximately half an hour. Fortunately, the Xiangge Police Station heard the alarm and ordered many police officers to rush to the scene to maintain order, which was well maintained. The details are recorded below:

Construction History

The Gonghe Cinema at No. 160, Fangbang Bridge, Minguo Road, was built in 1915. The owner is Pan Chongde Hall. At the time of construction, the scale was not grand, and the interior layout was also ordinary. However, it was the only one in the Chinese area of Nanshi at that time, so the business was still good. In recent years, major cinemas in the concession have been established one after another, becoming more and more beautiful and scientific. Zhang Zhenshan, the manager of the cinema, in order to survive, spent more than 20,000 yuan last year to repaint the building, replace the tables and chairs with new ones, and install sound machines, film machines, Panaton, and agents, etc., all of which were available. However, due to the economic downturn in all industries, the cinema's business finally declined. On the 24th of last month, it was subleased to a Cantonese opera troupe, which changed to performing Chaozhou opera. The rent was 2,000 yuan per month, and only night shows were performed, which started at 7:00 PM every night, and the audience was not crowded.

Sudden Fire Alarm

At 5:40 PM yesterday, black smoke suddenly emerged from the ceiling on the second floor. A child in the Cantonese opera troupe saw it and rushed to tell the accountant. Manager Zhang Zhenshan immediately reported to the Xiqu Fire Brigade by telephone. At that time, pedestrians stopped and traffic was interrupted. By the time the fire truck arrived, the fire had already broken through the roof, and the flames were soaring, making the fire uncontrollable. When the firefighters were setting up the hoses to connect to the water, the water tap on the side of the road suddenly ran out of water. It took more than ten minutes to draw water and put out the fire. This was all due to insufficient water supply.

Traffic Obstruction

When the fire was raging, about a dozen trams on Huashang Sanlu and French Concession Wulu in that area were stopped near the Chen Ying Shi Pagoda, like a long snake. Traffic was blocked for more than half an hour. Pedestrians gathered to watch, and the road was almost blocked. After the accident, Shen Zhenhua, the chief of the Shenxiangge Police Station in charge, ordered patrol officers and many police officers to rush to the scene to maintain order, which was very effective, so the order was quite good. When the reporter arrived at the fire scene, he saw the fire raging fiercely, with thick smoke like ink. Firefighters were busy working, and traffic was cut off, so he had to watch from the crowd.

Estimated Loss

Later, I learned that Zhang Zhenshan, the manager of the cinema, lived at No. 15, Shouxiangli, opposite the cinema, so I detoured to his house. According to him, the Gonghe Cinema had been open for nearly 20 years. This unfortunate incident caused a great loss, estimated at more than 100,000 yuan. It is said that if the entire Cantonese opera troupe was burned, it would lose about 100,000 yuan. It had insured for 10,000 yuan in fire insurance. The annual business was enough to cover the expenses. From June to the end of last year, it lost more than 6,000 yuan. From January to now, there is still a surplus. The daily income from playing movies, day and night, is about 200 yuan, and the daily expenses are only more than 80 yuan, which can cover depreciation and purchase of property.

Five Rooms Burned Down

The fire was extinguished by firefighters after burning for about two hours. As a result, five rooms were burned down, leaving only one corner of the ticket office floor. The accountant and two tea room staff were taken to the police station by the police on duty to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for verification.

Police to Increase Prosecution for Reckless Driving in Automobiles 121

Recently, the Public Works Bureau's Security Committee received a letter from the North China Automobile Insurance Association, advocating for limiting the speed of rental cars. According to the letter, rental cars on the market drive as fast as flying, especially on roads outside the concession. Speeds of 45 to 50 miles per hour are common, so accidents occur from time to time. Therefore, it is proposed that, because automobile accidents are very complicated, they cannot be judged solely on the basis of speed. If speed limits are set, accidents that occur can be regarded as extremely dangerous. However, in order to prohibit reckless driving of rental cars in the summer, avoid danger, and protect lives, the police can be ordered to pay close attention. If a car is driven too fast and is likely to cause danger, report it at any time and prosecute it. After careful discussion of this matter by the Security Committee, it was deeply felt that limiting the speed of automobiles is outdated today and is not suitable for modern needs. However, the measures proposed by the Acting Superintendent to ban dangerous driving are still feasible. It was immediately decided that the Superintendent should issue a notice to all police stations in the concession to pay special attention to the degree of danger of automobile driving and to report it at any time so that it can be detained. In addition to the above-mentioned rental cars, there are also cargo trucks and automobiles of the armed forces of various countries that often crash and disregard road regulations. These should also be paid attention to and notified to the headquarters of the armed forces of various countries to curb them. It is reported that the Board of Directors of the Public Works Bureau has approved and implemented the above items.

Police Continue to Crack Down on Trams Exceeding Passenger Limits, Three Measures Defined 122

Regarding the issue of trams and buses exceeding passenger limits, the Public Works Bureau's Security Committee held a meeting on the 25th of last month, and the Acting Superintendent reported on the investigation and crackdown results. According to the Acting Superintendent's opinion, the crackdown measures should continue to be implemented. On the one hand, whether trams and buses exceed passenger limits should still be strictly checked. Those with serious cases should be prosecuted, and those with minor violations should be given appropriate warnings. On the other hand, if tram companies or bus companies can take the following two measures, it will not be extremely difficult to comply with Section 1 of Article 36 of the traffic regulations. The so-called three measures are: (1) During peak hours for going to and from work, trams should drive straight without stopping or opening the door when they are full; (2) If a tram is full and passengers still want to climb on, the tram should stop and wait for the latecomers to exit before starting again; (3) Install a counting rotary machine so that the ticket seller can immediately stop the machine with one kick, and passengers will not be allowed to board again. As for whether there will be any inconvenience to passengers after the above measures are implemented, someone also asked about it at the meeting. According to the Acting Superintendent's view, if the companies can actively cooperate with the police, it will not hinder the convenience of passengers. After a general discussion, it was immediately decided to adopt the Acting Superintendent's proposal, continue to crack down on trams and buses exceeding passenger limits, check them at any time, and prosecute or give appropriate warnings to those with serious cases. It is reported that the Board of Directors approved the proposal a few days ago.

Shanghai-Taicang Long-Distance Bus Reduces Fares and Adds Special Buses 125

The Shanghai-Taicang Bus Company has been very considerate to passengers recently. It has already been convenient to shorten the distance and time between shifts. Now, it has also reduced the fares for the entire route and re-priced them, canceling round-trip tickets and coupon tickets. It is reported that the fare from Shanghai Station to Yuqing Bridge is 15 cents, to Dachang 21 cents, to Gujia Town 40 cents, to Liuhang 49 cents, to Luodian 69 cents, to Panjia Bridge 84 cents, to Liuhe 1.1 yuan, and to all stations directly to the Jialuo section, such as Shi Xiang Gong Temple, Xin Jing Bridge, and Jiading, are calculated according to the fare to Luodian. It is also reported that every Saturday, the last bus from Shanghai Station is extended to 5:30 PM, and a special bus is added at Jiading Station at 7:30 AM on Monday. All of this will be implemented from July 16.

The Kidnapping Case of Li Guanlin's Son: Kidnappers' Confessions Evade Responsibility; Interrogation Lasted Two Hours Yesterday; Case Still Needs Further Investigation 126

The case of Jinxiang, the four-year-old beloved son of Li Guanlin, a local villager residing on farmland at the Li family residence on Route Ratard in the French Concession, who was kidnapped for ransom on the evening of May 13th of this year, was solved by special agents of the French Police on June 21st. Thirteen kidnappers, including Zhao Shoutao and Chen A'er, were arrested successively. The victim was found in Jiangxinsha, Pudong. They were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and held in custody at the Police Department for detailed investigation and prosecution. This has been reported in this newspaper several times. The French Police have been conducting a thorough investigation of the suspects. Photographs of thirty-two men and women, including the arrested kidnappers and suspects, were presented to the mastermind, Chen A'er, to identify. He identified a total of thirteen people, including himself, and described the kidnapping, keeping the victim, and negotiating the ransom. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang Chaozuo of the Second Special Court, accompanied by Clerk Gao Yanmao, visited the First Criminal Court for interrogation. Lawyer Yao Zhaodi represented the French Police Department in court. Only Ding A'liu and Wang Jinxiang hired lawyer Zhu Dianqing to defend them. The court ordered the defendants to be brought forward and questioned them one by one regarding their names and origins. Lawyer Yao Zhaodi of the Police Department then elaborated on the case, stating that the first defendant, Zhao Shoutao, negotiated the ransom with Jin Sheng and Dong Aqing at the Han Bridge in Zhabei on June 21st. He also acted as a lookout during the kidnapping and confessed that the mastermind was the second defendant, Chen A'er, who is the brother-in-law of the victim, Li Guanlin. The third defendant, Wang Jinxiang, was also a co-conspirator in the kidnapping. The sixth defendant, Yang Shaobai, was also an accomplice to the kidnapping, and similar stationery used by the kidnappers to write to the victim for ransom was found in his house. The seventh defendant, Fang Dalang, provided the location to hide the victim. The eighth and ninth defendants, Su Zhaogen and Yang Hongde, guarded the victim in a thatched hut in Jiangxinsha, Pudong. Although they claimed ignorance, they were actually aware of the situation and should be considered accessories. As for the tenth, eleventh, twelfth, and thirteenth defendants, Ji Xiucheng, Xu Weiming, Jin Heshang, and Ding A'liu, all denied participating in the kidnapping during the investigation, but are suspected of providing assistance. They are now being prosecuted under Article 347 of the New Criminal Code for extortion through kidnapping. Subsequently, Detective Zhou Buguang, who handled the case, reported on the breakthrough and investigation process. After reviewing the report, the court ordered the defendants to be taken down for separate interrogations. The mastermind, Chen A'er, confessed that Jin Heshang and Ding A'liu were falsely accused by him and that he himself was also unjustly accused. At this point, the victim, Li Guanlin, testified that his brother-in-law, Chen A'er, had taken 250 yuan from him and entrusted a lawyer to send a letter to the police requesting the withdrawal of the detectives stationed at his house. The judge questioned Chen A'er about this, and he admitted to it, asking the court to expedite the sentencing of the defendants, insisting on implicating him, and refusing to reveal the truth unless he was imprisoned. The court, finding sufficient evidence of Chen's crime, urged him to confess truthfully, but Chen continued to be evasive. The court then brought forward the remaining defendants, who all denied participating in the kidnapping and claimed that they only knew that it was a case of a man and his wives fighting over family property and wanting to harm the child, asking for temporary shelter, which was consistent with their initial confessions. At this point, Police Inspector Qian Chenglong testified that the police had sent a detective disguised as the victim's representative to negotiate with the kidnappers on May 19th and had seen Dong Aqing and Yang Shaobai among the defendants near the Great World. The judge repeatedly interrogated the defendants for two hours but concluded that the case still needed further investigation and ordered a postponement to the morning of the 20th for further interrogation. The defendants were returned to custody.

Husband Missing for a Year; Wife and Son Sue Father-in-Law; Requesting Confirmation of Status; Judgment Awaits Pronouncement 127

Chen Yezhen, a Chaozhou native residing at No. 3 Huicheng Lane, Maidean Road, next to the Great Bell in the French Concession, is nearing sixty years old. He made his fortune by dealing in opium and accumulated substantial wealth. His brother is deceased, leaving behind a son named Fusheng, who was brought up by Chen as his own son. In the 21st year of the Republic of China, when Fusheng was nineteen years old, Chen arranged for him to marry Zhao (twenty-two years old this year), a woman from the same hometown, as his daughter-in-law. Less than a year after the marriage, Fusheng went out to do business and has been missing ever since, for three years now. Zhao gave birth to a son named Caifu after the marriage, who is now three years old. After Fusheng disappeared for a year, Chen drove Zhao and her son out of the house. As a weak woman, Zhao had no power to resist and had to take her son back to her mother's home. Chen refused to provide for their livelihood. Although Zhao repeatedly asked people to negotiate, no satisfactory resolution was reached. Therefore, Chen Zhao, along with her son, hired a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the Second Special Court against her father-in-law, Chen Yezhen, seeking confirmation of their status as his daughter-in-law and grandson. Upon receiving the lawsuit, Judge Ma Yishu summoned the parties to the Seventh Civil Court for questioning yesterday morning. The plaintiff, Chen Zhao, carrying her son Caifu, arrived with her lawyer and stated the case as described above. The defendant, Chen Yezhen, was represented by a lawyer, who denied the plaintiff's claim, stating that the plaintiff's husband was his nephew and that they had separated. He presented the separation agreement to the court. Judge Ma reviewed the evidence and, finding the facts of the case clear, ordered a debate and then announced the conclusion, scheduling the pronouncement of judgment for the morning of the 15th.

Closure of Stolen Snuff Case 130

Guo Zhongliang, a wealthy Chaozhou merchant residing in Shanghai, had three bottles of valuable snuff stolen from 20 Zhilan Lane, Route Cardinal Foch, on May 20th of this year. He immediately reported the theft to the police for investigation. After investigating the scene of the theft, the police suspected Zheng Taili, a Shantou native, and brought him to the police station for prosecution. Subsequently, the court found insufficient evidence of theft and acquitted him. After being acquitted, Guo Taili hired a lawyer to file a false accusation against Guo Zhongliang. The case was scheduled for judgment yesterday. The plaintiff did not appear. After taking the bench, the judge summoned Guo Zhongliang, asked his age and address, and then acquitted him in court, thus ending the false accusation lawsuit.

Four Banks Joint Treasury Issues Reserve Report, No. 288 131

The Four Banks Joint Treasury, established jointly by the Yien Yieh, Kincheng, China & South Sea and Continental Banks, is responsible for issuing banknotes for the China & South Sea Bank. According to the treasury's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with full reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for at most 40%. A public announcement is made weekly. The following is a copy of the Shanghai Treasury's 288th public announcement, dated July 6, 1935, as verified by the auditors and accountants of the four banks: Banknotes in circulation: 22,321,273 yuan; Total reserves: 22,321,273 yuan; Cash reserves: 17,380,373 yuan; Guarantee reserves: 4,940,900 yuan.

Honor for Qu Zhibu Hospital; Plaque Presented by Huang Jinrong 132

Chen Houzhi had been engaged in revolutionary work for many years and suffered from neurasthenia due to overwork. His condition was very serious and had not improved for several years. Initially, he could alleviate his suffering by smoking, but in recent years, he had become addicted to smoking, and his chronic illness not only failed to improve but worsened. He sought treatment from many doctors without success. Later, through an introduction, he entered Qu Zhibu Hospital for treatment and received careful diagnosis and treatment from Dr. Qu Zhibu, the hospital's director, and Dr. Yan Qingkang. He recovered completely in two months and had broken his opium addiction. His relatives and friends were very pleased and asked Huang Jinrong, a prominent figure in Shanghai, to write two plaques to present to the two doctors. The plaques read "Buddha's Heart, Saint's Hand (for Dr. Qu)" and "Profound Medical Knowledge (for Dr. Yan)." They were delivered to the hospital yesterday with military music.

Wu Ziyuan Reduces Price for Selling Calligraphy 133

Mr. Wu Ziyuan from Southern Anhui Province is proficient in calligraphy, especially the style of Su Changgong (Su Shi), which is rich and mellow, capturing its essence. He was highly regarded in Shanghai in the past. This spring, to expand his network of ink friends, he reduced the price for selling his calligraphy for one month in April. Those who sought his work came in droves, all wanting to obtain his ink treasures. Now, during this summer period, he often spends his time practicing calligraphy, so whether it is screen panels, couplets, fans, or albums, he is again reducing the price by half for one month to promote his art. Those who seek his work beyond this period will have to pay the regular price. Gentlemen at home and abroad who love calligraphy should not miss this opportunity. Price information can be obtained by writing to 339 Route Cardinal Foch, French Concession, Shanghai, and will be sent immediately.

Qian Zhiqing's Family Searching for Missing Person 135

Qian Zhiqing, an elderly man from Ningbo, residing at 6 Liyuan Guild Hall in this city, ran away from home a few days ago due to a minor incident and has been missing for many days. His elderly wife and children are neglecting their meals and sleep, searching everywhere, and their situation is very pitiful. His wife also stated that if her husband does not return within a few days, she vows to end her life. Currently, his relatives and friends are concerned about the tragedy of separation and are specially helping to search for him, hoping that the elderly man will resolutely return home to avoid the entire family perishing together.

Shanghai Statistical Supplementary Material Published 137

The Shanghai Municipal Local Association's Shanghai Statistics, compiled by the Shanghai Municipal Local Association, is divided into sixteen categories: Land, Population, Administration, Justice, Finance, Banking, Commerce, Industry, Labor, Transportation, Cultural Undertakings, Public Utilities, Education, Society, Health, and Agriculture. It can be said to cover all aspects of Shanghai's statistics. Since its compilation and publication in 1933, it has sold very well. It is now known that the supplementary materials compiled by the association in 1934 have also been published. Except for the Agriculture category, which has been temporarily suspended from supplementation due to the lack of significant changes after only one year of on-site investigation, the supplementary materials for the remaining categories are very rich and consistent with the old ones, connecting with each other. There are a total of 238 tables, priced at one yuan. Anyone who has purchased the 1931 edition of Shanghai Statistics must purchase these supplementary materials for completion. If purchased together with the previous edition, the price is even cheaper. The association, the Commercial Press, Shen Bao, Life Bookstore, and Author Bookstore all have them for sale. Those who want to study Shanghai must have a copy on hand.

Minsheng Fan Factory Relieves Unemployment 139

In view of the poor economic situation and the increasing number of unemployed people in the market, the Minsheng Fan Factory on Panjia Street, east of the Old North Gate, has specially sacrificed its own profits and reduced the price of its specially made New Life Group Fans, handing them over to the unemployed to sell, which can both promote the New Life Movement and relieve unemployment, a win-win situation. These group fans are beautifully designed, economical, and durable, and very easy to sell. Unemployed people have been flocking to buy them, and it is said that each person can earn an average of seven or eight corners of extra profit per day, which is a great benefit to the general unemployed.

Graduation Ceremony of Longhua Shanghai Orphanage 140

The Longhua Shanghai Orphanage was founded by Shanghai gentlemen Wang Yiting and Gao Fengchi and others and has been in existence for thirty years. Director Zhang Jifu is enthusiastic in his work, so the orphanage is thriving. The orphanage held its 22nd graduation ceremony at 2:00 PM on July 10th. Those present included Mr. Ji Hao, representative of the Municipal Party Department, Mr. Wang Shuxian, representative of the Wang Trustee, Mr. Gao Fengchi of the Gao Trustee, Mr. Lu Zhixue, Pastor Bao Zhaoqi, and more than 500 teachers and students. Director Zhang Jifu presided over the ceremony, led the attendees in a salute, and reported the number of male and female orphans and graduates admitted in the past thirty years, so that the guests could understand the situation in the orphanage. After the graduates sang the graduation song, the graduates gave speeches in Chinese and Western languages, and sang the orphanage song. Then, Mr. Ji Hao, representative of the Municipal Party Department, gave a speech, roughly saying that the country is now in a critical period of survival, and the country's survival depends entirely on your efforts, so you must be self-reliant and do practical work. He hopes that the graduates will be honest and law-abiding, not have too high expectations, and continue to read books in their spare time. The directors in the orphanage must study hard to save the country. Mr. Lu Zhixue's speech was roughly divided into three points: (1) The several directors of your orphanage are worthy of admiration, because it is not easy for a charitable organization to maintain itself for thirty years, which is entirely due to the directors' enthusiasm for charity. (2) The director has a spirit of sacrifice and service, so the achievements are remarkable. (3) The graduates working outside can bring glory to the mother orphanage. Finally, he praised the speeches of this year's graduates, which were well-organized and natural, which was very gratifying. Mr. Wang Shuxian's speech roughly said that the students can be so happy entirely because of the help of great benefactors. How should you repay this great kindness? I think that as long as you study hard, work diligently, and pay attention to the three educations of intelligence, morality, and physical education, and serve the society in the future, that will be enough. There is one more point, you must not forget the great benefactors who have created blessings for you. Pastor Bao Zhaoqi and Mr. Zhang Junkang gave speeches in succession. Then, Mr. Wang Shuxian was asked to present certificates. There were fifteen male graduates and six female graduates in this class. The graduates gave a thank-you speech, the staying students gave a praise speech, and the orphanage's band played music. The meeting was announced to be adjourned in the sound of music and photos were taken to commemorate the occasion.

Notice to Those Posting Advertisements in the French Concession 141

The French Concession authorities have recently noticed that various agencies, schools, and other public and private organizations in the concession post various advertisements without any restrictions, which will inevitably lead to malpractices in the future. Therefore, it has recently been decided that if various schools, agencies, and public and private organizations in the concession intend to post various advertisements, they must bring the number of advertisements and the establishment license of the organization or school approved by the French Concession authorities to the Police Department for verification in advance. If the above-mentioned license has not been obtained, they must complete the procedures according to the regulations before they can obtain permission to post advertisements.

Letters 144

To the esteemed editor: I am writing to you today regarding the news in the news column of your newspaper about the amateur drama club's volunteer performance at the Third Shanghai West National Goods Exhibition. Our troupe is the Amateur Friendship Drama Club. I believe the word "Friendship" was omitted during drafting. I am deeply concerned that the outside world may not understand and misunderstand. Therefore, I would like to correct it. Sincerely, to the news editor of this newspaper, Amateur Friendship Drama Club, July 11.

Respected editor: I am writing to you today regarding the news in the local news column of your newspaper, "Wife of the Hangzhou Restaurant Causes Havoc in the Auditorium." After investigation, Mr. Cheng Zhiliang is an unpaid assistant in our association, not a secretary, nor a performer of Shanghai opera. As for Mr. Cheng's marital dispute, Mr. Cheng is, of course, personally responsible for handling it himself and has nothing to do with our association. I am deeply concerned that the outside world may not understand and misunderstand. Therefore, I would like to issue a statement and correction, hoping that it will be included for your convenience and peace. Sincerely, Shanghai Shanghai Opera Research Association, July 11, 24.7.11.

Dear editor: I read in the local news column of your newspaper on July 11, an article about "Hangzhou Scholar Causes Havoc in the Auditorium," stating that "Cheng Zhiliang married into the Ding family, with me as the matchmaker." I am very surprised. After investigation, I have a teacher-student relationship with Cheng Zhiliang. In May of the Republic of China Year 16, when Zhiliang became the adopted son of Ding Quanlin, it was indeed introduced by me. However, the Ding family assumed that the adoption procedures were not completed. As for Zhiliang and Ding's younger sister (the fourth daughter of Quanlin) cohabiting, no wedding was held. Therefore, the marriage procedures have not been completed. The report does not match the facts. Please correct it in your newspaper immediately to avoid confusing the audience. I am very grateful. Sincerely, to the editor of Shen Bao, Zhang Junkang, July 11.

Sports News

Measures for Training Athletes in This City to Participate in the Upcoming National Games Were Approved by the Chairman and Members of the Selection Committee Yesterday; Training Will Begin Sequentially from the 15th of This Month 145

The preparatory committee for the preliminary round of the 6th National Games in this city held a joint meeting of the chairmen and members of the selection committees at 2:00 PM yesterday on the ninth floor of the YMCA in Baxianqiao. The "Measures for the Training Camp for Athletes in This City" were approved, and the dates and locations of various training sessions were decided. Details are recorded as follows:

Attending Committee Members

Including Jiang Jianbai, Shao Rugan, Wang Keyong, Hu Zongfan, Rong Qizhao (representing Wang Fudan), Zhang Guoxun (representing Lu Zhongen), Zhang Zizhen, Chen De, Ling Xitao, Ye Liang, etc., chaired by Standing Committee Member Jiang Jianbai.

Reporting Items

After the ceremony, the chairman reported: (1) The Education Bureau can allocate approximately 4,000 yuan for training expenses for each group after unified accounting. (2) For the sake of unified training, the Education Bureau has drafted the "Measures for the Training Camp for Athletes in This City" for discussion. (3) Please ask the chairmen and members of each group to formulate detailed rules for implementing training at all levels within the determined budget, according to the above measures. (4) This training is based on the principle of centralization. The main items in the detailed rules are training dates, training locations, standards for selecting athletes, nomination of instructors or managers, instructor subsidies, procedures for issuing athlete food and accommodation expenses, athlete supplementary selection dates, etc. (5) Instructor management, athlete subsidies, food, accommodation and miscellaneous expenses shall be unified by the Bureau's two-part receipt, in order to be uniform and facilitate reimbursement. (6) In addition to joining the training camp, each athlete should fill in an application form for membership. The method will be determined separately.

Discussion Items

(1) The draft of the "Measures for the Training Camp for Shanghai Athletes Participating in the 6th National Games" was amended and approved. (2) The training dates and locations of each group were decided (attached below). (3) The case of the detailed rules for the implementation of training by the Gu group was resolved that it should be drafted by the committee of each group and sent to the Education Bureau within one week. (4) The case of determining the registration date of each group was resolved that the method should be decided separately by each group and sent to the Education Bureau for public announcement. (5) The case of the candidates for instructors of each group was resolved that they should be nominated by the chairmen and members of each group and then selected and hired by the Education Bureau. (6) The case of the implementation method of football training was resolved that it should be decided after consultation with Committee Member Le Xiurong. (7) The case of determining the list of athletes who should receive training at all levels was resolved that it should be drafted by the selection committee of each group and then approved and announced by the Education Bureau.

Training Dates

The training dates and locations for each group are as follows: (1) Men's and women's track and field, starting from July 15, location: Jiaotong University. (2) Football, tentatively after August 15. (3) Men's and women's basketball, starting from August 1, location: Men's at Shenyuan, women's at Southeast Women's Physical Education School. (4) Men's and women's swimming, starting from August 1, location: YMCA on Sichuan Road. (5) Men's and women's volleyball, starting from July 15, location: YMCA in Baxianqiao. (6) Women's softball, tentatively starting from August 15, location to be announced later. (7) Men's baseball, tentatively starting from August 15. (8) Men's and women's martial arts, pre-selection training starting immediately, location: City Martial Arts Hall, Tianhou Palace Training Ground, and City Public Sports Ground No. 1. (9) Tennis, pre-selection on September 1, location: China Sports Association or Shanghai Tennis Club.

Training Methods

Measures for the Training Camp for Shanghai Athletes Participating in the 6th National Games: (1) The training camp will set up track and field, martial arts, basketball, football, volleyball, tennis, baseball, softball, and swimming teams. The director of the Municipal Education Bureau will hire a number of instructors and managers to be responsible for the conduct of the training. (2) The training period will be from July 15 to the end of September. Each team may make slight changes according to the situation. (3) Each team can be divided into three training periods. The first period will be two training sessions per week. After the end of the period, formal representatives will be selected to continue receiving training in the second period. From the third period, there will be three training sessions per week. The number of times can be increased by the instructors of each team, depending on the situation. (5) Officials and athletes will be subsidized for transportation, meals, and other expenses by the Municipal Education Bureau. (6) Responsibilities of instructors: (A) The training situation of the team members should be recorded in detail at any time. At the end of each training period, they are responsible for reporting to the Preparatory Committee together with the chairmen and members of each group for reference and review. (B) In addition to being responsible for technical training for the team members, special attention should be paid to sportsmanship and strict training should be carried out. (7) Matters that team members should pay attention to: (A) Abide by all rules. (B) Absolutely obey the management of each position. (C) Should be given practical training in sportsmanship. (D) After being selected to participate in training, they should not be absent without reason or withdraw halfway. (E) Should not be absent for more than one-fifth of the prescribed training time. In case of unavoidable accidents, a legitimate reason must be stated and leave must be requested in advance. (8) The formal lineup of representatives of each team will be reported to the Preparatory Committee by the chairmen and members of the selection committee of each item by the end of August at the latest, and will be publicly announced after deliberation and approval. (9) During the training period, the Education Bureau will send personnel to inspect separately at any time and handle the matter together.

In addition to the team members participating for free, people from all walks of life are welcome to participate. Special municipal ferries and public buses will be rented for pick-up and drop-off. The ticket sales locations are the Liangyou Bookstore and Magazine Company at the intersection of North Sichuan Road, and the Guangdong Swimming Team on the third floor of No. 1316 North Sichuan Road. However, due to the ferry cabin capacity, the team members and guests already exceed 200 people, so the number of tickets sold is limited to 100. At that time, in addition to inviting the mayor, the heads of various bureaus, and celebrities to the venue for guidance, sports reporters from various newspapers will also be invited. The invitation cards have been sent out yesterday by the Shanshi-run Seaside Bathing Beach. The public carnival tickets are limited to 100 due to the car space problem. However, the news had just been revealed the night before, and six-tenths of them had been removed within an hour. Yesterday, a certain Guan Ti sent a letter to the team, requesting an increase in the number of places in order to prepare for the entire participation. After receiving the letter, the team replied after consideration that the boats and cars were limited. Qingyanggang Railway Garden Hotel saw news reports that the team planned to hold a message in Wusong or Qingyanggang. The night before, they sent a letter to the team to express their welcome and expressed their willingness to provide the team with various conveniences from the standpoint of promoting sports. Captain Li was very sorry that he received the letter too late and had made an appointment with the Seaside Bathing Beach in advance. In order to avoid embarrassing the kindness, it is planned to hold a wild swimming competition or a rowing competition in Qingyanggang next month.

Education News

The Ministry of Education Revised Short-Term Primary School Textbooks 156

The short-term primary school textbooks compiled by the Ministry of Education were originally intended for out-of-school children aged 10 to 16. Recently, the Ministry of Education promulgated the "Provisional Regulations for One-Year Short-Term Primary Schools," changing the age of enrolled children to 9 to 12 years old. Therefore, the textbooks also need to be revised. The Ministry of Education has ordered the National Compilation and Translation Bureau to revise them. It is also heard that the Compilation and Translation Bureau has sent Wang Weixin and Hu Yanli to be responsible for the revision based on the newly revised "Provisional Curriculum Standards for One-Year Short-Term Primary Schools" and the words used in the "Primary School Elementary Vocabulary Grade 1-2" compiled by the bureau. New life movement and air defense materials will also be added appropriately, and it is expected that they will be completed within the month for application when school starts in the fall.

The Compilation and Translation Bureau Responded to the Revision of Ministry-Compiled Textbooks 157

The National Compilation and Translation Bureau recently submitted to the Ministry of Education, stating that it had previously received orders from the Ministry to revise the Ministry-compiled primary school textbooks. The original manuscripts included one copy each of elementary Chinese, social studies, nature, and arithmetic, and one copy each of advanced Chinese, geography, history, nature, and arithmetic, for a total of nine copies. Except for the two copies of advanced geography and history, which were found to be inapplicable after review and investigation, they have been submitted to the Ministry for record. There are many shortcomings in the contents of one copy of nature. After detailed signature and annotations, please transfer and instruct the original compiler to revise it. Chinese and arithmetic are still under review. The elementary Chinese consists of eight volumes, the first volume has been revised and is ready, the second volume will also be finalized soon, and the third volume and below are also in progress. The focus of this revision of Chinese is: (1) to pay attention to our country's inherent morality, etiquette and materials for the revival of the nation; (2) to take children's daily life as a starting point and avoid the disadvantages of falsehood and mythology; (3) to suit the conditions of ordinary rural areas and not to focus on urban life; (4) to apply the biological materials in nature, pay attention to their living conditions, and their relationship to people; (5) the distribution of content, style, and quantity is based on curriculum standards; (6) the new words used are checked against the elementary primary school vocabulary compiled by the museum; (7) the compilation uses a single method to connect each lesson from beginning to end, etc. As for the elementary social studies, there are four volumes for the third and fourth grades. The original manuscript has been revised many times and is currently being reorganized. There are four volumes for the elementary nature for the third and fourth grades. After the revision, it has been sent to various experts for review and revision, and it is currently in the final finishing stage. After the elementary arithmetic of eight volumes was reviewed, it was decided to revise it. The first four volumes were revised in the museum, and the latter four volumes were handed over to the original compiler for revision. A revision plan was also formulated: (1) Take children's actual life as the center; (2) Pay attention to ruralization and popularization, and make full use of production materials; (3) Make full use of simple materials such as labor, nature, social hygiene, etc. to achieve mutual connection; (4) Make full use of various recent statistics; (5) The words used should be compared with the elementary primary school vocabulary compiled by the museum; (6) Use a unit compilation, and each volume cannot have two or more units with identical facts; (7) The first volume is mainly based on pictures, and the pictures should focus on saving, being clear and easy to understand, using less background, and avoiding the disadvantages of complexity and chaos; (8) The pictures also focus on popularization and make full use of common things in the school and family environment; (9) The arithmetic games used in low grades should focus on those that are easy for general schools and children to implement. Now the first volume has been revised and completed. All the situations since February when the ministry-compiled primary school textbooks were ordered to be revised have been reported for review. It is now found that the elementary primary school Chinese Volume 1, the mimeographed version has been printed and is ready to be sent to various experts for review. Please find one copy and submit it for review and instructions.

The Ministry of Education Ordered the Selection of Students Studying Abroad to Pay Attention to the Level of Foreign Languages 160

(Nanjing, 11th Dispatch) The Ministry of Education ordered all halls and bureaus: According to regulations, students applying for the national-funded study abroad examination should have a considerable foundation in the language of the country where they are going to study. Those who replace the language of the country where they are going to study with the language of another country at the time of application because their language proficiency in the country where they are going to study is poor should also have full reading and writing ability in the language of the country they are replacing. When sending national-funded students to study abroad in the future, special attention should be paid to the foreign language proficiency of these applicants. Those who fail in this subject should not be admitted. I hope you will follow this order.

Inquiry into the Principal of Wujin Women's Normal School 165

Wujin County Women's Normal School, established since the late Qing Dynasty, has a history of thirty years. It has long enjoyed a reputation in society, especially in the recent five years, since Mr. Zhuang Minqiu took office as principal, there has been considerable progress. During Mr. Zhuang's five-year term as principal, he saved money within the extremely tight regular expenses, and strived for construction, both materially and spiritually. Therefore, in recent years, although the Wujin Women's Normal School receives less than 10,000 yuan in public funds per year, which is less than one month's expenses for provincial schools, its appearance and actual staff can be compared with provincial schools. The current principal, Zhuang Minqiu, found it difficult to maintain the school because the school's funds were discounted by the local education bureau, coupled with huge arrears. In addition, he suffered from insomnia due to years of hard work. Therefore, he once submitted his resignation during the spring vacation, which was approved by Qian Hao, the head of the education bureau, with the comment "No discussion for the time being". Since Mr. Zhuang could not leave for the time being, and his health gradually recovered, he took on the responsibility for the school's financial difficulties alone, and became actively responsible for school affairs. Recently, on June 21st and 25th, Director Qian inquired about his attitude twice, and Principal Zhuang made a positive and responsible statement. At 4 pm on June 29, the school received an order from the Department of Education, stating that according to Director Qian's report, the principal "still has the intention to leave", and the resignation should be approved. After receiving the order, Mr. Zhuang prepared to hand over his work. However, all sectors of the local community, as well as the school's alumni, faculty, and students, sent urgent telegrams to retain him, and sent representatives to the province to petition. The provincial authorities are now planning to send personnel to investigate the truth.

Zhang Yuanruo Lectures on Chinese Rule of Law Issues - At the Education Bureau's Summer Training Class - 169

Law expert Zhang Yuanruo lectured on Chinese rule of law issues at the Municipal Education Bureau's summer training class yesterday and today. The content includes (1) the theoretical basis of the principle of rule of law, (2) the factual advantages of the principle of rule of law, (3) the reasons for the failure of the rule of law in China, and (4) the ways to construct the rule of law in China. Based on China's national conditions, he widely quoted various theories, and each point developed extremely valuable opinions. He also stated that if we want national rejuvenation today, we should first enrich the strength of the country, and especially strengthen the national organization. This cannot be achieved without actively promoting the spirit of the rule of law. The lecture lasted for more than two hours, and more than 800 students listened attentively in the hot summer and took notes. They were in good spirits. After the lecture, all the audience applauded to express their respect.

Special Article: The Past and Future of the National Sino-French Industrial College (2) 174

- Chu Minyi

In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, the school was closed due to student strikes. At that time, it was a pity that undergraduate students dropped out of school midway. Minyi then consulted with the Ministry of Education to send the students to study in Belgium, divided into two batches of twenty people each. The cost of studying abroad was subsidized from the school's funds. At the same time, the school's funds were quite tight, but we tried our best to economize. Fortunately, the students were able to work hard in Belgium and lived up to their expectations, studying day and night, and even on Sundays. Therefore, there was a saying that "Chinese people have no Sunday." Therefore, many of them ranked first in foreign universities and won glory for the motherland. Now, all the students have returned to China after completing their studies and are serving in various sectors of the country, mostly in construction. They occupy important positions in various ministries and commissions of the central government, as well as in the construction departments of Guangxi, Shandong, and Hebei provinces. Their service achievements have been praised by the authorities of various agencies, which is very gratifying. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, the Sino-Belgian Gengkuan Committee was established, and students were sent to Belgium. At that time, seven students graduated from the school's high school department, so they were able to participate in the examination and were sent to Belgium by the committee. Now, the students have also returned to China after completing their studies and have their own tasks. Last year, eight students graduated from the school's first graduating class. Among them, the top two, Hua Yigan and Zhou Jiamu, were also sent to Belgium by the Sino-Belgian Gengkuan Committee, Sun Yutai and Jin Sangzhang were subsidized by the Sino-French Education Fund Committee to go to France, and Cheng Fuzhu was admitted to the Ministry of Education's government-funded program to Italy. The rest were introduced by the school to work in various places. This year's graduation examination is being held. After the students graduate, we will still find a way for them to find a way out, so that they can all get what they want.

(3) Future Plans

The school building is still spacious. Some of the houses are lent to the Sericulture Improvement Association and the Sino-French University School of Pharmacy, and some of the houses are temporarily occupied by French soldiers. The part occupied by French soldiers has now been recovered. The Sericulture Improvement Association and the Sino-French University School of Pharmacy are working together on the Sino-French cultural cause, and there is currently no news of relocation. Once a residence is found, the houses will be returned, and the school can strive to expand, such as establishing a research institute, so that students can continue to study advanced industry after graduation, and adding an affiliated junior high school, so that junior high school students can directly enter high school after graduation and complete the two-level middle school system, so that the curriculum can be connected. In the future, if the school's funds are slightly sufficient, the factory laboratory and library can be enriched and expanded. Regarding the way out for students after graduation, we will still follow the previous policy, so that those who are both virtuous and talented can go abroad to study and create advanced industrial talents. We are currently discussing with the Sino-French Education Fund Committee, hoping to send several students to France to study every year, to promote the actual communication of education and culture between China and France.

Today, internal and external troubles have reached their extreme, but with such national strength, even if Guan Zhong and Yue Yi are reborn, what can they do? If we blame and demand perfection and only rely on empty words, it is enough to mislead the country. Only by being persevering, united as a country, burying our heads in hard work, and striving for construction to seek production, can we continuously strengthen ourselves and perhaps survive. And construction is inseparable from talent. Therefore, we can only do our best and strive for this. (End)

Commercial News

Finance Foreign Banks Increase Prices but Underlying Market Weakens Silver Futures Fall, Then Briefly Rebound 175

—Resulting in a Drop of Six Yuan and Seven Jiao—

Yesterday, although foreign banks uniformly raised their prices, the underlying market softened. This led buyers to take advantage of the low prices, resulting in a rebound after the fall. The Hong Kong market also loosened before tightening slightly. However, the Indian market contracted before rebounding, while the Hong Kong market remained loose, ultimately ending weak. Early in the morning, overseas silver markets in England and America were generally lower, but it was said that buyers were content, fearing high prices and a lack of buyers, leading to a weak market. The forward silver price in Montreux rose by only 2.5 to 5 li, and exchange rates all contracted. London raw gold rose by four pence. When pre-market trading opened, prices initially dropped to 33.34 yuan, but buying was eager, pushing them up to 34.45 yuan before more selling occurred. When the Central Bank announced its official rates, both English and American rates rose, while the customs gold unit fell by seven li. The benchmark gold standard price was listed at 868.8 yuan, opening slightly lower, but rebounding after the opening. Banks showed little appetite, and sellers took the opportunity to operate, making it difficult to sustain the gains. It was anticipated that the HSBC's listed rates would show an increase of 125 for English and 25 for American rates. Prices then fluctuated and fell, with selling pressure intensifying. Reports from Hong Kong also indicated a firm market, which was very weak for a time. However, as the Hong Kong market soon softened, sentiment calmed, and prices gradually rose. Banks traded among themselves, and the domestic market gradually tightened, leading short sellers to cover their positions, stabilizing the trend. Later, Reuters reported that Indian silver futures for July were expected to rise by five annas, stimulating buying and causing a rebound. The market was stable at noon, but later reports indicated that Indian silver futures had contracted by 4.33 annas, causing slight disappointment. The off-market trading immediately became flat and weak, but rebounded slightly after opening. Banks showed little appetite, and a second report indicated that Indian silver futures had rebounded by six annas, but soon went downstream again. However, there was some fluctuation after the low, but sellers continued to operate, and the Hong Kong market also hardened, ultimately leading to further declines. A third report from Indian silver indicated a rise of one anna and no change, with little impact. The Hong Kong English exchange rate had loosened to 2 shillings and 2 pence 0.0625, but the underlying market remained firm, ultimately ending weak. The market was volatile throughout the day, and sentiment followed the Hong Kong market. Short sellers offered 1.5 yuan for the next term (August to September), which was previously predicted to be around 4 yuan. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was 833.3 yuan, a decrease of 5.6 yuan from the previous close. Fu Xing Yong Yong Li Lai Jin rose to 5.3 yuan, while Heng Yu Fu Yu Hui Xiang Wan Chang Yong Da De Cheng Da Fa Yong tax fees fell to 1.8 yuan. Fu Yu Yong Huan Xiang Yuan Chang Yong Yi Feng Yong took advantage of the low prices to make up the difference, rising to 3.9 yuan. Mitsui came out offering a shilling 125. It was anticipated that HSBC's listed rates would increase by 25 for English and 25 for American rates. Fu Xing Yong Da De Cheng sold, lowering the price to 2.7 yuan. The situation fluctuated, and later Hui Xiang Fu Xing Yong Heng Yu came in, causing prices to rise to 5 yuan. Huabi sold August shillings 875. The asking price for cargo from this company was 16 yuan and 5 fen, and there were few sales. The asking price for Taigu sugar B mark lacked acceptance, and the No. 1 domestic cotton white sugar, at 15 yuan and 3 jiao, also showed signs of weakness. The domestic cotton red, which had been selling relatively actively recently, had its previous market slightly loosened, but demand from all parties increased again, so yesterday's market tightened again. High-quality goods opened at 11 yuan and 6 jiao, and ordinary goods opened at 11 yuan and 6 jiao, with 200 and several tens of bags traded. It is said that there is not much inventory left.

How Much Is A Person Worth? 188

— Pei Yu

"How much is a person worth?" This question is difficult to answer correctly. For example, someone who has done great things in a spectacular way and made great contributions and benefits to society and humanity, is difficult to calculate. Someone who is mediocre and does nothing, who cannot benefit humanity in life and has no impact on society in death, is worthless, impossible to calculate. If we estimate the value of a person by how much money they can earn, then an inventor who has spent a lot of effort inventing something that benefits humanity will get far less money than a popular celebrity who sings a few songs and dances a few times. This valuation is still incorrect. If you want to value it correctly, you must use chemical analysis. Using chemical analysis to analyze the human body, the result is very accurate and fair. Because everyone, regardless of rich, poor, noble, humble, intelligent, stupid, good, or evil, is the same.

According to a report by Dr. Lawson of England, the average value of a human body is five shillings (approximately 2 yuan, 6 jiao, and 5 fen in Chinese currency). This is because the human body contains enough water to fill a ten-gallon bucket, enough fat to make seven long bars of soap, enough lead to make nine thousand pencils, enough phosphorus to make two thousand two hundred match heads, enough magnesium to make one dose of salt, enough iron to make a medium-sized nail, enough lime to whitewash a chicken coop, and enough sulfur to remove fleas from a dog.

A Method to Escape the Heat - Swimming 189

— Hua Ling

The weather is getting hotter every day. Hot, hot, hot. Electric fans, soda, ice cream - nothing can get rid of the threat of heat. Lying down, sweat still oozes out like it does on a damp cement floor, damp and sticky, uncomfortably.

But don't panic! I'll tell you, there are good places to go. In this city, there are swimming pools, and, well, beaches.

Although I am not a pampered son from an ivory tower, since I grew up in the countryside from childhood, and when I was about ten years old, I followed my brother, carrying wooden doors, and playing in the small river. Therefore, even though I have drifted into the city now, somehow when I mention swimming, I will be happy from the bottom of my heart. It is especially because of the cramped living conditions that I feel more need for this pastime.

Therefore, every summer, I almost always have to rush to Hongkou Park to swim whenever I have free time. In recent years, in our company, during the hottest two or three weeks, we work in the morning and rest in the afternoon. So I use this free time to imitate the Yangzhou people's "afternoon water bathing," soaking myself in the swimming pool.

Since last year, I have often taken the city ferry, crossed the river, and gone to the Gaoqiao beach. The reason is that the Gaoqiao beach is not only spacious and has soft sand, but what makes me linger is the gentle and very cool sea breeze blowing from the Pacific Ocean. What's more, when the sun, which can blister people's skin, is swallowed by the city, I climb out of the sea onto the beach, stretch out my limbs, and lie down, welcoming the evening breeze. At that time, not only do I feel unlimited ease, but I simply forget that this is in a summer with a temperature of over ninety degrees.

Although life is so unfortunate, fortunately, there are places to swim, so I can survive such a long, hot summer. Otherwise, well, who knows, I might have been driven crazy by that long, hot summer.

On the Hill 190

— Yan Bokuang

On the hill, there is a stretch of lush green grass, abundantly spread on the warm yellow mud. On this grass is a small house surrounded by red and white striped curtains. Behind the house is a cluster of green bamboo. The weak light of the setting sun shines through the sparse gaps in the bamboo leaves onto the delightful face of the heavenly maiden. Two dark eyes glance at the four men with different expressions and smiles on their faces. A long pine bench holds a jar of oily rotten bamboo shoots, several packs of delicious beef, and Wujiapi wine is poured into the stomach like boiling water. A jar of honey-soaked lychees, she slowly sips the sweet juice.

The cause of this kind of enjoyment is less about admiring the green bamboo and more about using alcohol to numb the pain, right? But what kind of taste will they feel after they wake up from the alcohol?

After the wine and dishes are finished, several drunkards all propose to leave this beautiful hill. No, the hill is not beautiful, the beauty is still on the girl. On the way back, they talked about the emotions of longing after last night's farewell. She and I were walking side by side, passing by a long riverside, a small stone bridge, a high mound, and a narrow ridge. The girl was wearing a long blue dress mixed with azuki bean-colored flowers. The embroidered shoes under the beige stockings aroused - surprise - frequent glances. When I return to Shanghai later, I will tell you about a fun place to live.

The girl's movements, posture, and beautiful Shanghai language are constantly floating in the minds of the four men. The most valuable rendezvous on the hill is a scene in the history of life worth remembering forever.

Dreaming of Crying for Yu Cen 192

— Fang Jiekan

Yesterday, you were interred, and relatives and friends all came to mourn. Only I was busy with wedding preparations, and Lanling looked wistfully into the distance. Last night I dreamed that you came to say goodbye, leaning on the bed, sitting, talking, and laughing. Holding your hand, I felt it was still warm, but your appearance was very withered. An old woman sat to your left, and her appearance was very similar to yours. Her white hair was full of her head, but her red face was so bright. She said she was your grandmother, and a secluded residence was being built. A pot of soup and medicine was placed on the table, and the steam surrounded it like clouds. Suddenly, I remembered that your illness was critical, and who would take care of everything. I was comforting you, holding back tears, when I woke up and the sky was not yet dawn. Alas, Xie Yucen, your clear posture was always outstanding. Why didn't Heaven bless you? Your talent was abundant, but your life was short. Your poetry and prose were famous early on, and your calligraphy and painting followed Ni Zhao. In your spare time, you enjoyed epigraphy, and your appraisal was also excellent. For ten years, I have been lucky enough to be a close friend, and we have studied and discussed academics with each other. I think of me as a guest in Shanghai, poor and worried, and people easily grow old. I carve seals to support myself, and I cannot avoid the slander of the world. I am grateful that you alone saw my good points, and you always spoke kindly to me. When you were bedridden, you repeatedly informed me by mail, saying that seal carvers are mostly long-lived, and told me one by one. You bought stones and asked me to engrave and send them, but your heroic spirit has already disappeared. When I unfold the letter, the ink is still fresh, and I shed tears in vain.

World Rare News

Octogenarian Great-Grandmother Receives Bachelor of Arts Degree 194

— Special

On June 8th, at the commencement ceremony of Claremont Colleges in Los Angeles, USA, among the graduating students who were mostly handsome young men, there was also a petite old lady with a height of five feet and a kind smile. She was Mrs. Guist, an octogenarian who was already a great-grandmother. Sixty years ago, she had already graduated from Illinois Woman's College (now renamed McKendree University) and obtained a Bachelor of Arts degree for women. At that time, universities generally did not award bachelor's degrees to women, but now that men and women are equal, she was able to receive a Bachelor of Arts degree at this graduation ceremony. When she bowed to President Blaisdell to receive her diploma, her blue eyes sparkled, causing people to laugh. Three of her eight children attended the ceremony. Later, she said to others, "I don't want my children to be ashamed of me. Three of my sons have already received degrees. I don't like to hear them say, 'Mother is very capable, she can bake very good cookies, but...' you understand." "But I can also cook." During her year of study at Claremont Colleges, she wrote a 28,000-word thesis titled "Lucretius: A Naturalist Poet." This paper was based on six research areas: two in the history of philosophy and the other four in Greek archeology, Roman history, Roman literature, and Latin. She proudly told people that she had never missed a day of school throughout the year. She lived in a small room in the Saycamore Lodge, which was simply furnished, like many other female students. The only difference was that they all had pictures of many boyfriends hanging up, while she had pictures of her children, grandchildren, and great-grandchildren, both male and female. She once said to her classmates, "These young people can remember things after reading them two or three times, but I am old and must work twice as hard to remember. I study for at least five hours every day, and up to eight hours." She also said, "Once I have decided to do something, I will naturally be satisfied when I succeed, but my pursuit of knowledge is only to prevent my children from running ahead of their mother. I have wanted this degree for many years, and it is only now that I have obtained it." Mrs. Guist was born in Ashtabula, Ohio, USA, on November 15, 1854. In 1876, she married Reverend Guist, a professor of English at the West Virginia Normal School in Fairmont. The couple lived in Fairmont for thirty-five years. In 1908 and 1909, leaving only two sons at home, Mrs. Guist pursued literary research and later obtained a Bachelor of Arts degree from Cornell (Iowa) University's Board of Trustees. After Mr. Guist passed away in 1932, Mrs. Guist traveled to California, Hawaii, Florida, and other places. She had eleven children, eight of whom are still alive. This old lady's tireless pursuit of knowledge is truly rare in the world.
