Free Talk

The Development Process of a Novel 195

— Qu Yi

Anyone with creative experience probably knows that before starting a piece of work, one must go through a painstaking process of thinking: how to depict the personality of the characters in the work, how to arrange the background, how the story develops... only when the work has been fully arranged in the author's mind, can they begin to write. Writing in this way, at least the author can get some degree of satisfaction. As for the impact on readers and society, that is of course not something the author can calculate. This depends on the author's understanding and grasp of social reality. But for the author to accurately grasp and understand social reality, that is not within the scope of creation; it belongs to the author's personal life. Let's leave that aside for now.

But sometimes, even though the author has arranged everything properly, once they start writing, they completely or partially overturn the original plan; even the opposite result comes about. Even the author themselves cannot predict it and has to let the writing run wild. I think anyone with creative experience must have experienced this. The best example is a passage of self-confession in Fadeyev's creative experience; he said:

"When I was writing *The Rout*, for the first time I encountered that many of the things I had conceived before were not incorporated into the work. I encountered new elements that emerged in the work process that I had never thought of before. For example, according to my original plan, Mechik was going to commit suicide in the end, but when I started writing this character, I gradually became convinced that he could not end in suicide, nor should he."

"After drafting the outline of the protagonist's behavior, psychology, appearance, expression, etc., as the novel develops, this or that protagonist seems to correct the original design themselves, and there seems to be a logic of their own in the development of the characters. To give an example: it is one thing for Mechik to live in a military hospital and in the forest; it is another thing for him to join the team after he gets better. I tried to imagine how he would act in the new situation, and therefore I got another result. The protagonist of the work, if the artist knows him well, leads himself to some extent."

This passage is truly insightful. Those who have never tasted the joys and hardships of creation cannot say such a thorough thing. But we cannot completely say it as mysteriously as Fadeyev, saying that when the novel develops to a certain stage, the characters in the novel can lead the author to go in the direction of his own suitable voice and appearance. In fact, this is all related to the author's own consciousness. Taking Mechik in *The Rout* as an example. The author originally planned for him to end in suicide. Of course, Mechik did not want to be given a positive evaluation in the author's conception, so he used suicide to deny the value of his actions. But when the novel developed to a certain stage, the author's correct consciousness, in constant self-examination, felt that ending Mechik with suicide would instead make him feel somewhat lovable. So let him escape. Once Mechik escaped, the rogue nature of Moroska increased in value on the other hand; and all the characters in *The Rout* were even more powerful. On the surface, it seems that the protagonist in the work is indeed leading the author. In essence, it is still the author's correct consciousness that leads himself. In other words, the author discovered, from the premise of using suicide to deny the value of Mechik's actions, that this negation of suicide was not powerful; and might even cause readers to sympathize with the suicide victim; therefore, he more powerfully used escape to deny the value of Mechik's actions. But the author's essential plan to give Mechik a negative evaluation was still not changed.

Early Chinese New Literature authors often used the word "inspiration" as the only proper attitude for creators. Therefore, most of the novels at that time were in the form of essays. There was no need to pre-arrange any development process for a work. They mostly said that their articles came "from shaking the pen" and "were completed in one stroke." Undoubtedly, this creative attitude has long been negated. If an author is still so proud now, it is not showing the development of his creative genius, but confessing his egoistic indulgence. Then came an opposite advocacy, which was the so-called content issue of the work, making the works of that period dry and tasteless. Now, of course, many authors have corrected this incorrect tendency. But some people also argue that the work does not necessarily have to pay attention to its development process. This seems to be open to discussion.

To continue writing down a realistic prototype of a section, there should also be a vague organic connection in each fragment; but in my opinion, this kind of novel only achieves the first step of displaying the material. Just as when we read some novels by certain writers, we often think of pieces of bloody meat on a meat pillow. There is naturally some partial realism in its expression. However, it is definitely not vivid. This is, of course, a subjective choice made by the author; but without consciously giving it an organic connection. In other words, this kind of technique by the author ignores the causal pursuit of each phenomenon.

Every novel does not necessarily have to have a complete story. Every work must pay attention to its development process. And this development process must not be scattered piece by piece without connection. In its development process, it is necessary to pay attention to its causality and give it a positive or negative evaluation.

China's Goddess of the Sun and Moon 196

— Yao Xueyin

Greece and Northern Europe both have beautiful myths. China also went through a primitive era, and probably had them originally, but unfortunately most of the myths were lost later.

Yi shooting the ten suns is one of the surviving beautiful myths, but it is not very complete. I have previously collected all the materials about this story from books such as "Heavenly Questions," "Li Sao," "Classic of Mountains and Seas," "Huainanzi," and "Zuo Zhuan" to conduct a comparative study, and as a result, I unintentionally discovered the goddess who gave birth to the sun and moon. And what is interesting is that the goddesses who gave birth to the sun and moon were originally twin sisters, the well-known Ehuang and Nuying.

In ancient times, according to Guo Moruo's "Research on Oracle Bone Characters," the myth of the ten suns was produced among the Xia and Shang peoples who had some knowledge of farming. Originally, barbarians saw the sun rising and falling, and thought that the sunset was the sun's rest, and that the one that came out from the east the next day was the second one. This speculation is very reasonable. They guessed that the sun had ten brothers, who took turns in charge of the daytime; later, the ten brothers came out together, scorching the crops, plants, people, and animals to death, so God "gave Yi a red bow and white arrows" to shoot and kill nine of the suns. This God was Emperor Yao in the Xia nation and Emperor Shun in the Shang nation. Ancient books record places where there were multiple suns in the sky, such as:

"There is a Fusang tree in Tanggu (i.e., Yanggu), one sun arrives and one sun comes out, all carried by crows." (Classic of the Great Wilderness: East)

"There is a Fusang tree in Tanggu, where the ten suns come out. It is north of the Black Teeth, located in the water, with a large tree, nine suns residing on the lower branches, and one sun residing on the upper branch." (Classic of Lands Within the Seas: East) "The Ruo tree is west of the Jian tree, and at the end are ten suns, whose brilliance illuminates the ground below." (Huainanzi: Topographical Instructions)

"When King Wu attacked Zhou... when fighting, the ten suns were in chaos above." (Ibid: Military Strategies)

"In the eighth year of Emperor Lian, there was a monster, and the ten suns came out together." (Bamboo Annals) "The ten suns come out in turn, melting gold and scorching stones." (Summoning Souls)

In addition, in the twenty-ninth year of Jie, two suns came out together, see "Bamboo Annals" and "Weft of the Classic of Filial Piety"; in the fifth year of Jianxing of Emperor Min of Jin, three suns shone together; "Book of Tang: Turkic Biography": five suns came out together, illuminating for three months in a row. However, the myth of ten suns in the sky is the oldest and most widely known.

Regarding the birth of the ten suns, the "Classic of the Great Wilderness: South" says:

"Outside the East Sea, between the sweet waters, is the country of Xihe; there is a woman named Xihe, who bathes the sun in the sweet abyss. Xihe is the wife of Emperor Jun, and she gives birth to the ten suns."

According to recent research: Emperor Jun is Emperor Yan, that is, Emperor Shun. Shun's wives are traditionally Ehuang and Nuying. "Xi" is pronounced "E" in ancient times, and "Huang" and "He" have the same sound, so Xihe should be Ehuang. Therefore, the "Classic of the Great Wilderness: South" also has the saying "Emperor Jun's wife Ehuang gave birth to this country of three bodies." Therefore, I think it would not be a mistake to say that the goddess who gave birth to the ten suns is Ehuang. As for recognizing Nuying as the goddess who gave birth to the moon, the evidence is as follows:

"Emperor Jun's wife Changxi gave birth to twelve moons." (Classic of the Great Wilderness: West)

"Emperor Ku's second concubine married a woman of the Zi clan named Changyi." (Chronicles of Emperors and Kings)

Changxi is the same as Changyi, which is Chang'e. Yu is Shun, and Shun's second concubine is Nuying, so Nuying is Changyi, later written as "Chang'e" or "Heng'e." "Classic of Lands Within the Seas: North" says: "Shun's wife Dengbi gave birth to Xiaoming Zhuguang, living in the great swamp of the river. The spirits of the two daughters can illuminate a hundred li in this direction." This is a trace of the two concubines giving birth to the sun and moon. Probably the name Nuying came later. In the original legend, Shun's two concubines were not Ehuang and Nuying, but Xihe and Changyi. Later, the myth was historicized, and Xihe and Ehuang were split into two people, the former becoming the sun driver; and also split into the Xi clan and the He clan, as Yao's two ministers. Nuying ran out for no reason, squeezing Chang'e out of Shun's side and turning her into the wife of Yi who stole the elixir and fled to the moon. The story of Chang'e fleeing to the moon is related to the alchemists of the Qin and Han dynasties and is very clear.

Raffles Place 197

— Fei Er

Singapore Impression Notes III

Every day, Raffles Place is neatly lined with many modern cars, and the tall buildings on both sides constitute the heart of the entire Nanyang region. Foreign money constantly flows in and out from here, and the entire Nanyang colony is tightly held in the pens of high-ranking officials.

In the morning and evening, cars and trams are filled with people coming and going. Newspaper vendors shout at the top of their lungs, and foreign language newspapers are discarded on desks or held under arms.

At noon, as soon as the banks and foreign firms close, the Indian bosses stick out their big bellies and direct their black employees to greet customers in their coffee shops. As a result, the coffee shops are immediately filled with many races: white, yellow, black, and brown. At the same time, the coffee shops are filled with the smoke of hot food, cold drinks, and cigarettes. Malay and Malay-style English, occasionally mixed with a bit of Indian and Chinese, flow out in a torrent, turning the entire coffee shop into a cacophony.

Choosing a quiet corner of the coffee shop and quietly observing the faces of these various people from all over the world (regrettably, the red race is missing), seeing how each character that constitutes Nanyang's "Wall Street" uses a posture to express that they are a small piece of the capitalist machine, is quite interesting.

Until the dark night, Raffles Place is left with only a sense of calmness and desolation. The banks and foreign firms have tightly closed their iron doors, the bookstores selling popular English and American magazines only display the covers of various interesting books in the windows; the Chinese pupils who supply the daily necessities of the foreign firm employees have stopped shouting and selling their goods, and stacks of invoices have also been put away. The Indian gatekeepers snore on their cots, while the "matas" (Malay policemen) lonely tread their weary steps, and the moon casts cold silver light from the tall corners of the walls. Raffles Place is like a desolate castle surrounded by cement. When calm, Raffles Place is deserted, and only the sea tide near the coast stirs up the roar of the waves in the late night.

The daytime noise and the nighttime silence are the regular contractions of the heart of Singapore. When the foreign firm employees also curse their "London homeland," and when the tide of recession also sweeps into Raffles Place and causes them to lose their jobs or have their salaries reduced, Raffles Place suffers from anemia again. Then, Raffles Place will gradually fade its intense color, and the special impression it leaves on people will gradually diminish.

University Days (22) 198

— Written by Storm of Germany, Translated by Chen Yinzhi

I was in a state of confusion when suddenly I heard the little girl say a low "Good night!" Then I saw her disappear into the shadow of the portico. I heard the sound of the door carefully opening and the faint sound of the doorbell. Then I turned around and slowly walked home through the mansion's garden.

I didn't go to my parents' living room for dinner, but sneaked upstairs to my room. I lay on the mattress as if drunk. After a quarter of an hour, I heard the door move; from the half-closed seam of my eyes, I saw my mother approaching my bed with a lamp. She bent down towards me, but I closed my eyes tightly and continued to dream. Although she didn't give me much hope when we parted tonight, I felt as if my hand had already grasped a rose-colored ribbon and was walking towards a happy future.

I wanted to think silently alone that night, and the next morning I wanted to run into the crowd. I had a new feeling of freedom and victory, and now I wanted to perceive this feeling in front of others. After I finished breakfast and reluctantly answered a few troublesome questions from my mother, I went to my friend Christopher's workshop. He was intently selecting small pieces of mahogany wood to carve. "What are you making something good?" I asked.

"A sewing box," he said, without looking up.

"A sewing box? For whom?"

"For Lena Se. Borica's; my sister wants to give it to her as a birthday gift."

I watched him from the side; a smug smile appeared on my face. "Is Lena your sweetheart, Christopher?"

This good young man blushed with shame at my presumptuous question. He seemed angry at his own embarrassment. "You guys should let her out of your Latin dance school!" he said, angrily splitting the wood with his knife.

"Are you really jealous like this, Christopher?" I asked.

But he didn't answer; he just muttered to himself, "If it were my sister, then..."

But this time, the matter was only my one and only time of success, because no matter how I tried to find ways, I never had the chance to be alone with Lena. During the summer, she met me several times on Sunday afternoons on the sidewalk behind the garden, but Christopher and his sister accompanied her. This good young man walked proudly next to her, as if he wanted to fight the "Latins" for her; she herself seemed to urge them to move forward and not talk to me when I went to talk to them.

When Getting off the Train 199

Crossing the Yellow River at Night 200

— Qi Wuwen

In this short period, I ran to many small places and crossed the Yellow River twice. It was simply not a journey, but a gallop, a transfer. Only the white clouds in the west wind were more elusive than me!

That's right, life is always on the road, and I am even more on the road within the road.

One night, I took the Pinghan train south, and when I arrived at the north bank of the Yellow River, I ran out of the carriage to the place where people were getting on and off, leaned on the iron railing, and waited to personally experience the night scene of the Yellow River.

A long and sharp whistle swept through the wind, and the huge Yellow River iron bridge was in front of me; followed by the heavy metallic sound of the wheels and rails rubbing, adding a bit of emptiness and slow meaning. What I saw first was a vast expanse of shallow yellow and grayish sand, and even after more than thirty sections of the bridge, there was only sand under the bridge. The moon could not be seen in the gray sky, and the sparse stars were covered by a curtain woven of fine sand, appearing and disappearing in the northwest wind. Under such a sky, the beach spread out silently like a soft Dead Sea, and the lights of the iron bridge illuminated the heavy and orderly shadow of the iron bridge, and the heavy shadow of a row of trains, pressing down on this sea.

Finally, I saw the river itself. The water seemed not deep, and its turbid yellow color could still be distinguished under the light! A color a little more yellow than the sand. The wind seemed a little tighter than before, and the machine's voice could not cover the rhythmic sound of the river water splashing against the shore. The closer to the center of the river, the faster the water flowed, and white eddies surged. The river was empty, only in the distance where the river and the starry sky were about to meet, a jagged dark shadow was lit up. From that slender, towering pole-shaped object, I recognized it as a boat. In such a dark night, in such a classical river, such an ancient boat was parked alone. "Is it an eerie dream?" I couldn't help but be led into fantasy by this picture full of melancholy suggestion. I remembered that I had vaguely had many dreams similar to this picture. Sometimes I felt that it was the dark shadow of "fate," and sometimes I felt that it was a symbol of "despair." After waking up, I often felt an inexplicable terror. And now I was actually in this similar realistic realm—and precisely in the windy storehouse of the vast future ahead, how my subconscious mind was throbbing at that time!

The Yellow River was crossed in a short while, followed by another vast beach. I didn't return to the carriage until the iron bridge was over. I felt a little chilly and rubbed my cheeks, which were also icy cold. It turned out that I had been standing in the wind for almost half an hour.

"Knowing that this time will definitely be crossed again, what about the hundred feelings before Zunqian? It is also something that has never happened in this life, crossing the Yellow River with a chest full of clear tears!" Isn't this one of the miscellaneous poems of Gong Ding'an Guihai (1833)? I first read Gong Ding'an's poems because of a friend's strong recommendation. That friend once asked me what I liked to read most. I remember that this poem was what I especially liked at that time. I loved its white depiction, I was moved by its twists and turns, but I always felt that its sadness was a bit exaggerated. I never thought that I would actually be in the realm of the poem, and the sadness seemed to be equally exaggerated. This accidental coincidence is worth my reflection.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Italian Reporter Demands Duel with British Member of Parliament 201

— Meng Ruo

Among the current group of self-proclaimed civilized people, many barbaric customs are still often left over. For example, dueling is one example. Dueling often arises from love disputes between men and women or disputes over certain events. The methods of dueling are sometimes sword fighting and sometimes gun fighting. When dueling, in addition to the two duelists, it is also necessary to invite a second to witness the event. This kind of behavior, as we see it, is barbaric, but they say it is civilized, because the duel is voluntary on both sides and there are rules of dueling to be followed. In reality, this may be a little more civilized than assassination.

According to recent news from London, an Italian Fascist newspaper reporter, Captain Faurelli, claims that he is willing to duel with Major Attlee, the deputy leader of the British House of Commons. Faurelli said that he is willing to compete with Attlee in a neutral country with any weapon, because he objected to Attlee's recent reservations during the debate on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute in the British House of Commons, so he has this determination. It is said that Attlee has refused, saying that dueling is a barbaric and evil custom for resolving disputes, and he does not deign to do so, but Faurelli is still dissatisfied and is determined to do it.

The feelings between Britain and Italy were not bad, but recently, because of the dispute over the Italian-Abyssinian issue, a rift has occurred between the two countries. Initially, the ruling leaders of both sides issued tit-for-tat remarks, accusing each other. Later, public opinion also followed, attacking each other with harsh words. Unexpectedly, now there is an Italian newspaper reporter who claims to want to duel with a British major. This is also an aspect of the deterioration of relations between Britain and Italy.

Objectively speaking, Faurelli's desire to duel with Attlee stems from patriotic ideology, rather than from personal grudges. However, this kind of behavior is too extreme. Attlee's refusal is not a sign of weakness; he simply does not deign to do so. It is said that when Attlee met with a Reuters reporter to talk about this matter, he said that Italy has no freedom of speech today, so Faurelli does not know what is permissible during debates in the British Parliament. I wonder what Faurelli thinks of this remark?

Flute Sound 202

— Hua Zhi

The moonlight of summer nights is like pure white milk, like a gentle and quiet virgin, pouring into my lonely window; every day my weak body is worn down by heavy work, and on moonlit nights, I greedily yearn for her tenderness and tranquility, turning off the electricity and lamps, and smoking a light cigarette by the window. The light summer breeze, like a mother's love, caresses my face, and I stare blankly as the wisps of smoke float upwards, feeling as if I am dissolving into this harmonious and peaceful environment, completely without thought, often forgetting the time for sleep.

For a week now, the light breeze of each night has carried a mournful flute sound. Although I don't understand music, I like it, but that weeping flute sound stirs up endless sorrow in me!

Every night I listen intently, trying to discern its direction. The suburbs are so quiet, and the residents all sleep early, except for the croaking of frogs, and the flute sound of that unknown person; but even if I listen with all my ears, I can't tell which direction it's coming from. For days now, my mood has been disturbed, and I haven't had a moment of peace. I go to bed late every day, almost doing so just to listen to his flute sound.

— Does that unknown person have unspeakable hidden sorrows? Or perhaps he's stirred up a deep homesickness? On this moonlit and breezy night, he pours out his sorrows through the flute. But has he ever considered that there is someone like me (and perhaps more sympathizers) whose painful memories are evoked by his flute sound? I've also thought that he might be a free-spirited poet, searching his barren mind for a poem on such a beautiful moonlit night. Unable to find a satisfactory work, he uses the flute to inspire his poetic mood, but why doesn't he play a happy tune? One should be optimistic in life!

But tonight, as I think of him, the flute sound I expected doesn't come. I also sensitively think that perhaps he's gone mad; or perhaps he's wandered off to another unfamiliar place, but I don't want my ideal to be like that; I'd rather hear his low, mournful flute sound again tomorrow night!

Then, a pale face flashed before me; it was a classmate from middle school, whom I met through playing the flute.

— One holiday evening, I went to bed early. But I was surrounded by a strange feeling of being attacked, preventing me from falling asleep immediately. That was the first time I heard the flute sound. It was a classmate from next door, playing his phoenix flute, and I couldn't sleep because of the low, mournful sound, so I banged loudly on the wall, signaling him to stop that wretched thing.

But unexpectedly, he shouted, "Friend, come over and sit for a while."

As if receiving an order from a superior, my anger completely dissipated. I put on my bathrobe and involuntarily went to knock on his door. The person who opened the door was a young classmate whom I saw every day but had never greeted. From what the other classmates said, he was very aloof; even those in the same dormitory rarely saw him smile. He was always alone. But today, I found a trace of warm smile on his thin face, and he warmly shook my hand, but his hand was cold.

— I'm sorry we've never spoken before. Why aren't you going home on the holiday?

— Go back to where?

— You don't have a home? That's just as pitiful!

Spurred by sympathy, we became friends at first sight. We became very close friends. For the last few years, we lived in the same dormitory, although my friends warned me that it was dangerous for me to get close to such an eccentric person.

But we graduated safely. On the night of our farewell, we shook hands earnestly and parted ways. The days have passed so quickly, and it's been five long years now, but I haven't heard any news of him or received a single word from him.

Why has tonight's flute sound suddenly stopped? He might be that lonely friend of mine. Even if it's someone I'll never know, I still hope that he's not as unfortunate as I imagine!

— Hu Kao

Rainy Day Vendor—Haven't even made fifty cents today!

Dream 203

— Liang Qijun

I like dreams.

I believe that anyone who is imprisoned by the shackles of reality will say that they like dreams.

Dreams can give people comfort; although this comfort is temporary, and it disappears like a flash in the pan. But if you dream of something you've been pursuing day and night without success, how happy would you feel! At least, you'd be able to crack a smile in an extremely gloomy atmosphere. However, afterwards, perhaps due to excessive joy, you'd feel a slight disappointment, and you'd say:

— Ah, it's a pity it was just a dream!

The beauty of dreams is extremely beautiful, so peaceful and light. It's like in spring, in that increasingly warm season, the falling petals of blooming, vibrant peach blossoms landing on the still stream, causing slight ripples, gently caressed by the spring breeze, slowly spreading out in all directions. And then, gradually, disappearing at some unknown time and place.

I don't remember which translated work said in the translator's preface that Russians are the best at dreaming. So, I read that book again and again, and I don't know if it was influenced by it? I love to dream now.

Dreams are close to fantasy. Because I often yearn for the loveliness of places like the Caucasus, Spain, or Hawaii. So, after reading novels or watching movies about these places, some fantasies arise——.

"A southern tropical island, a bright moon hanging in the pale ink-colored sky, coconut trees casting huge, beautiful black shadows intertwined on the grass, lying alone under a [blank space] tree, quietly listening to the natives playing passionate and provocative music with a primitive flavor,..."

"Or in an antique castle town, listening to Spanish-style tunes, men, bullfighting gladiators, women, wearing unique dresses, beautiful and melancholy faces with a hint of a slight smile,..."

That night, perhaps, dreams about these things will quietly come.

Page 20

Watching the Rain 204

— Lin Xi

Of all the rain I've seen in my life, the most interesting to watch has been in these three situations: on a steamship, on a train, and when I was a child at the doorway of my home. It seems that the scenes of childhood are always worth cherishing, but many of them don't mean much when I think about them now. Maybe it's because my mood has changed; the feeling of watching the rain at my doorway is gone now. Maybe it's because my family's circumstances are too bad to allow a grown-up to act like a child at the doorway anymore. So, this kind of rain-watching can now only be savored in memory, but there's not much real interest in it anymore.

As for watching the rain on a steamship or a train, that's for grown-ups. Being able to see a rain shower amidst the hardships of travel can really bring a sense of warmth to a traveler. In many places, it can even evoke a traveler's loneliness, but that loneliness is sweet, moist: at least, that's how it is for me. I've never tasted the flavor of "Clear and Bright Festival, rain drizzling," so I don't know. But from the perspective of the time, those travelers on the road are really in a poem: following the shepherd boy's hand, watching the apricot flowers in the rain from afar, that misty scene, one would say they were drunk rather than heartbroken; even if they were drunk with loneliness, it's also sweet, [blank space]. If this were on a boat or train, one [blank space] could be lonely enough to fall asleep, which is much better than listening to the dry [blank space] crashing sound, which is much more boring. Much sweeter. When [blank space] is boring, a thin [blank space] is a sleeping pill [blank space] [blank space] [blank space] can be [blank space] that is [blank space] , one can wash away boredom. Falling asleep while watching the rain is an admirable thing. When I was a child, sitting at the doorway of my home, swinging my legs, humming an unknown song, watching the wind carry the rain drifting past the coconut leaves, drifting past the misty fields, I would often lean against the wall and fall asleep; although I don't have that opportunity now, nor that mood, it's still sweet and moist to think about. This kind of rain-watching is now only a memory! The real enjoyment of watching the rain is on steamships and trains.

Watching the rain on a steamship always feels a bit like a lonely boat being battered by the rain, so just saying "watching" doesn't seem to be enough; one has to listen too. Watching is good, the mistiness of the sea can really make someone who gets lost in it jump down; and listening is even more interesting. It's rhythmic, the mechanical sound of the ship traveling is the rhythm, very even, and most people who have been on a ship probably know this. In each rhythm, there is the sound of wind and waves, it is a very grand march, with the so-called earth-shattering momentum; yes, passengers will feel lonely in this momentum, but that rare momentum will make passengers forget themselves, forget the dryness and boredom; they will "forget their form" in loneliness. The "beauty" of the scene can pull people into the scene, which is perhaps what is called "becoming ethereal." Watching the rain can make people reach such a point.

Rain must be very captivating. The third-class carriage should be the most boisterous. When I say boisterous, I still mean the travelers' minds, watching the telephone poles receding one by one, who isn't calculating how far away they are from their home? Originally, going out is really a hardship, with anxious and bored minds. Looking around, there's not a single familiar face. Your own words can only be [blank space] in your own heart; a tired face showing tired thoughts. Facing each other, you just pretend to look at the scenery outside the car, and no one can guess what the person opposite is thinking. This is so boisterous, so annoying! But seeing the surroundings drooping, gloomy, this atmosphere of suffering will naturally dissolve; seeing the crops outside the window swaying, that scene of the mountain rain about to come, almost forces every passenger to say that the rain is coming. "Yes, the rain is coming!" The person opposite will also answer, and then they will start talking, and a third person will add, "Close the window!" In this way, strangers are no longer strangers. This is the effect of the rain, making the traveler's heart warm. When the conversation dies down, they turn back to watch the rain, watching the rain hitting the crops outside the window, looking at the trees in the distance, at the horizon. [blank space] passing through the village, the villagers are also taking their children to the doorway to watch the rain! Watching, watching, the heart will become blurred, and there is no time to calculate how far away from home! Leaning on each other, some are absorbed by the rain! What's left is the rhythm, the sound of the wheels grinding against the rails.

Watching the rain is so interesting. But it may be my sorrow that that kind of rain-watching as a child is gone. I can only taste a little flavor in my memory, and although the flavor is good, unfortunately, I'm grown up, and I don't have the mood to reminisce much anymore.

Movie News

Beautiful Little Women 208

People call Chen Yanyan "Beautiful Little Bird" because she recently starred in "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River," wearing a gorgeous Western classical-style dress, so people call her "Beautiful Little Women."

Kathleen Hepburn starred in "Little Women," and her attire was almost the same as hers. When Yanyan dresses like this, she looks even more beautiful and quiet. Precisely because of this, the photos she took in this outfit have recently been used as covers by several film magazines in Shanghai.

According to director Ma Xuweibang, the reason for letting Yanyan wear this kind of clothing in "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River" is not to be innovative, but to consider the performance. As for what kind of performance effect this clothing has, we can only wait to see the film.

Ying Yunwei's Whole Family Acting 209

"Heroes of the Times" was filming Shang Guanwu's 50th birthday that night. Because the scene was too large and there were too many actors, only half of the eighteen shots planned were filmed. Last night, everyone was mobilized again to film the remaining nine shots.

The lively situation that night was the same as the previous night, but four more guests appeared among the five hundred congratulatory guests: one was a fashionable modern lady, and three were lively and innocent children. These four guest performers attracted the attention of everyone on the set. It turned out that this "modern lady" and the three children were the wife and sons of director Ying Yunwei. That night, their whole family made a cameo appearance in "Heroes of the Times." Their expressions were all natural. Cinematographer Zhou Keyou commented, "The wife and sons of a famous director are extraordinary."

Zhao Dan and Shu Xiuwen's Ups and Downs 210

Zhao Dan, this young man with a pretty face, his every move makes people feel good about him. His acting skills are not only very successful on the screen, but also excellent on the stage. Last time, the amateur drama club performed "Nora," and Zhao Dan played the role of Helmer in it, with truly captivating expressions, and was called an actor with "ghostly" talent by a certain director.

Because of his love for drama, Zhao Dan gathered his drama-loving comrades in the Mingxing studio the day before yesterday, preparing to organize a drama group, and expressed his opinions on drama, saying that drama is the only tool to transform society, so if we are determined to change society, we must start with drama. His comrades applauded enthusiastically, and Shu Xiuwen was even happier, embracing him passionately. But just as they were about to kiss, director Zhang Shichuan shouted "Cut," forbidding their actions, which was a great damper on the atmosphere, so this good thing was abandoned. Later, after asking the onlookers, it was learned that they were filming a scene in "The Big Family."

"Muddleheaded Gentleman" Released 211

This is a big joke about that Hollywood Mr. Nice Guy being mistaken for "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde." His name is Charles Butterworth, who once flaunted his wealth by tearing up thousand-dollar bills in "The Hollywood Revue." His humorous style can be called unique. Now he has become a "Muddleheaded Gentleman," dropping a tear gas at movie fans. (Note: This tear gas is actually a joke.) The female lead is the comedic star Una Merkel. It is produced by MGM, and is now released in Nanjing. On the left is the side-splitting "Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde" scene.

It is said that after these two films are completed, Tang may leave the film industry. If so, "Little Angel" and "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River" will be Tang's last works.

Sun Yu's wife is ill and is being treated by a famous doctor. Sun's new work, "Go to Nature," has had its model made by the set designer, and key staff and actors may be gathered in the coming days to discuss the plot and set a shooting date.

Lianhua recently received a slapstick script from a Ms. Lin Mengjuan, titled "Playing the Flute to Attract the Phoenix," depicting the love of a madman and showing the ability of humor and satire to the extreme. It seems to be the same flavor as Chaplin's "City Lights." If it can be made into a film, it must be starred by [blank space] Langen.
